Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Imam Sanusi's Pioneering Role in Aqeedah
Introduces Sanusi's leadership and the centrality of his works in aqeedah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Sanusi is considered the central figure in classical aqeedah and how his works came to dominate the field.

Core Idea
Sanusi’s works became the standard—master them, master the field.

This passage from a classical aqeedah coursebook explains the towering status of Imam Sanusi. It describes how his works became the reference for later scholars, making mastery of his books essential for anyone studying Islamic theology. The author also praises Sanusi’s elegant style, contrasting it with the difficult prose of later writers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Sanusi's centrality in aqeedah.
2
Identify the claims
Notice the three claims: Sanusi's leadership, dependence of later works, and stylistic superiority.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why mastery of Sanusi's works makes other kalam texts easy.
4
Consider the contrast
Compare Sanusi's elegant style with the 'stony phrase' of others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لقد كان للإمام السنوسي في القرن التاسع الهجري ريادة بارزة في علم العقائد ؛ حتى آلت رايتها إليه ، فعكف الناس تحت لوائه واتَّخذوا من كُتبه مفزعاً يفزعون إليه ، حتى إنَّ الناظر ليرى أن جلَّ الكتب المؤلفة من بعده عالة في أكثر سطورها عليه ، فمن أتقنها فقد أتقن هذا الفن ، وما وراءَها من كتب الكلام فلن تعسر عليه مطالعتها ، على أنَّ رشاقة العبارة وبعد مرماها في معناها أحبُّ إلى الطالب من عبارة حجريَّة يمضعُها فلا تلين ، وبهذا يظهر فضل السابقين على اللاحقين
Imam al-Sanusi had a prominent pioneering role in the 9th century AH in the science of beliefs (ʿilm al-ʿaqāʾid); until its banner passed to him, so people gathered under his protection and took his books as a refuge to which they flee, so that the observer sees that most of the books authored after him are dependent upon him in most of their lines. Whoever masters them has mastered this art, and beyond them of the books of kalam will not be difficult for him to study, given that the elegance of expression and its deep reach in meaning are more beloved to the student than a stony phrase which he chews but it does not soften. And by this appears the merit of the predecessors over the successors.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage introduces Imam Sanusi and his authoritative position in the field of aqeedah (ʿilm al-ʿaqāʾid). The author states that by the 9th century AH, Sanusi had taken the leading role, so much so that scholars and students turned to him and his writings as their primary reference. The text asserts that most later works on the subject are dependent on Sanusi's writings in most of their content. Mastering Sanusi's books therefore gives mastery of the entire discipline, making other kalam texts easy to study. The author also praises Sanusi's style: his expressions are elegant and profound, unlike the dry, difficult prose of others. This contrast highlights the superiority of earlier scholars (like Sanusi) over later ones.

Key Terms
السنوسي
علم العقائد
الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Later kalam works are independent and original.
Correction: This passage shows that most later works are dependent on Sanusi's writings.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the relationship between later kalam books and Sanusi's works?
A) They are completely independent.
B) They are largely dependent on Sanusi's works.
C) They are superior to Sanusi's works.
D) They are easier than Sanusi's works.

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi’s works form the foundation of later aqeedah scholarship—mastering them is key to the field.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you guilty of relying on modern summaries and secondary sources while neglecting the foundational works like those of Imam Sanusi? What concrete step will you take today to return to the core texts of aqeedah?
?
The passage praises Sanusi's elegant expression over 'stony phrases.' When you find a text difficult, do you give up or complain, or do you persist until it 'softens'? What does your reaction reveal about your commitment to sound learning?
?
Sanusi's books became the standard against which all later works are measured. In your understanding of Islamic creed, what is your yardstick? How can you be certain that your beliefs are built on the same solid foundation as the early scholars?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi
The biography lists the full name, lineage, nisbas, and scholarly titles of Imam al-Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage, nisbas, and key attributes of Imam al-Sanusi.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi was a master theologian, Maliki jurist, and Ash'ari theologian.

This lesson introduces the biography of Imam al-Sanusi, the author of our text. The passage lists his full name, his many scholarly titles, and explains the meanings behind his nisbas. Understanding who he was helps us appreciate the weight of his theological work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's words set the stage.
2
Identify the key titles
Look for titles like 'Shaykh of the theologians', 'muhaddith', 'muqri', 'faqih', 'usuli', 'Sufi'. Notice the range of his scholarship.
3
Understand the nisbas
Focus on 'al-Maliki', 'al-Ash'ari', 'al-Tawhidi'. What do they indicate about his school of law, creed, and specialization?
The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' refers to his expertise in the science of tawhid.
4
Note the lineage and tribe
His name includes his lineage. The nisba 'al-Sanusi' is explained as coming from a Berber tribe. His mother was a sharifa.
5
Connect to his authority
Reflect on how this biography establishes his credentials as a reliable authority in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي
شيخ متكلّمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدّث؛ المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع التلمساني
أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي
المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي
والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في «تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية (١) ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية (٢) ، ووجد بخطّهِ على ( شرح الآجرومية » له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف « : القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى (۳)
والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي
Translation of Imam al-Sanusi: The master of the theologians (mutakallimin) of his time and region, the imam, the all-knowing scholar, the muḥaddith, the muqri', the jurist, the foundational scholar (uṣūlī), the investigator, the Sufi, the pious, the abstinent, the Tlemceni. Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawḥīdī. Al-Sanusi: a relative attribution (nisba) to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in Taj al-'Arus: 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi because he settled among them, and it is said he is actually from them, and his mother is a noble Hasaniyya (descendant of Hasan), as verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Mallali in al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya. And it is found in his own handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-'Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar'. I say: al-'Isawi is from the house of 'Isa. And al-Tawḥīdī: a relative attribution to occupation with the science of tawḥīd (divine oneness), as mentioned by al-Ḥifnāwī.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biography (tarjama) of Imam al-Sanusi. It opens with his honorific titles: 'Shaykh of the theologians (mutakallimin) of his time and region', 'Imam', 'Allama', 'Musharik' (participating in multiple fields), 'Muhaddith', 'Muqri' (Qur'an reciter), 'Faqih', 'Usuli' (specialist in fundamentals of jurisprudence), 'Muhaqqiq' (investigator), 'Sufi', 'Taqi', 'Wari' (pious, abstinent), and 'Tlemceni' (from Tlemcen). Then it gives his full name: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi. His madhhab (school of law) is Maliki, his creedal school is Ash'ari, and he is also called al-Tawḥīdī. The passage then explains the nisba 'al-Sanusi': it comes from Sanusa, a Berber tribe in the Maghreb. It cites al-Zabidi's Taj al-'Arus, which says the attribution is because he settled among them, or that he was actually from them, and that his mother was a sharifa (noble descendant) from the line of Hasan. It also mentions a note in his own handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajrumiyya where he writes 'al-Sanusi al-'Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar'. The biographer comments that 'al-'Isawi' means from the house of 'Isa. Finally, it explains 'al-Tawḥīdī': it is a nisba to occupation with the science of tawhid (divine oneness), as mentioned by al-Ḥifnāwī. The biography establishes the Imam's scholarly pedigree and his commitment to Ash'ari theology.

Key Terms
سنوسي
مالكي
أشعري
توحيدي
مُحدِّث
مُقرِئ
فقيه
أصولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The nisba 'al-Tawḥīdī' indicates a separate sect or Sufi order.
Correction: The text explicitly states that 'al-Tawḥīdī' refers to occupation with the science of tawhid, not a separate group.

Checkpoint
What does the nisba 'al-Tawḥīdī' refer to according to the biography?
A) A Sufi order
B) A tribe in the Maghreb
C) Occupation with the science of tawhid
D) A place name in Tlemcen

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi was a towering scholar of Ash'ari kalam, Maliki fiqh, and Sufi piety, whose works remain authoritative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are given the honorific 'Shaykh of the theologians of his time'. What would need to change in your pursuit of knowledge for you to be described similarly in your community—not by comparison to others, but by genuine mastery?
?
The Imam is described with multiple titles: muhaddith, muqri, faqih, usuli, sufi. Do you have a narrow focus, or are you striving for comprehensive Islamic knowledge? This week, what is one concrete step you can take to learn a field you have neglected?
?
His mother was a sharifa, indicating a family line of piety. Consider your own family: what legacy of knowledge and faith are you building for those after you? Is your current daily routine contributing to that legacy or distracting from it? What one habit can you start today to make a lasting impact?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
The Biography of Imam al-Sanusi
Sanusi's biography introduces his full name, nisbas, and titles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly pedigree and key identifiers of Imam al-Sanusi, including his name, titles, and the meanings of his nisbas.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's titles reflect his mastery across Islamic sciences.

This lesson introduces the author of our text, Imam al-Sanusi. Before studying his theological work, it is essential to know who he was, his scholarly standing, and the meanings of the names used to refer to him. The passage from the commentary provides a detailed biography that highlights his expertise and lineage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify components
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note that it begins with his titles, then gives his full name and lineage, then explains each nisba.
The passage is dense with honorifics; don't get lost in details.
2
Examine the list of titles
The passage lists several titles: master of theologians, imam, all-knowing scholar, muḥaddith, qāriʾ, jurist, uṣūlī, pious, ascetic, god-fearing. Each indicates a field of expertise.
3
Understand 'al-Sanusi'
The nisba 'al-Sanusi' is explained through a quote from al-Zabidi, linking to a Berber tribe. Note the discussion about his lineage.
His mother was a noble Ḥasanī, adding sharif lineage.
4
Note additional nisbas
From his own handwriting, we learn additional nisbas: al-ʿĪsī, al-Sharīf, al-Qurashī, al-Qaṣṣār. The author comments that al-ʿĪsī means from the house of ʿĪsā.
5
Reflect on 'al-Tawḥīdī'
The last nisba is explained as relating to the science of tawḥīd. This is significant because he is known for his works on creed.
Misconception: it is not a sectarian label.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي. شيخ متكلّمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدّث ؛ المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع التلمساني أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي. والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في «تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية » ، ووجد بخطّه على شرح الآجرومية له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف : القرشي القصّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى. والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي.
Translation of Imam al-Sanusi. The master of the theologians of his age and his country, the imam, the all-knowing scholar, the muḥaddith, the qāriʾ, the jurist, the thorough uṣūlī, the pious, ascetic, god-fearing al-Tilimsānī, Abū ʿAbd Allāh Muḥammad ibn Yūsuf ibn ʿUmar ibn Shuʿayb al-Sanūsī al-Mālikī al-Ashʿarī al-Tawḥīdī. Al-Sanūsī: a relative attribution to Sanūsa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. Al-ʿAllāma al-Zabīdī said in Tāj al-ʿArūs: 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abū ʿAbd Allāh Muḥammad ibn Yūsuf ibn ʿUmar ibn Shuʿayb al-Sanūsī because he settled among them, and it is said he is from them, and his mother was a noble Ḥasanī,' as verified by Sayyidī Muḥammad ibn Ibrāhīm al-Mallālī in al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya. And it was found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ājurrūmiyya: 'al-Sanūsī al-ʿĪsī al-Sharīf: al-Qurashī al-Qaṣṣār.' I said: al-ʿĪsī: from the house of ʿĪsā. Al-Tawḥīdī: a relative attribution to engagement with the science of tawḥīd (divine oneness), as al-Ḥifnāwī mentioned.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage opens the biography (tarjama) of Imam al-Sanūsī. It lists his lofty titles: 'master of the theologians of his age and his country', 'all-knowing scholar', 'muḥaddith', 'qāriʾ', 'jurist', 'thorough uṣūlī', 'pious, ascetic, god-fearing', and his full name and lineage. It then explains his nisbas: al-Sanūsī is attributed to the tribe Sanūsa, with a discussion from al-Zabīdī about whether he was a descendant or a visitor. It also mentions a note in his own handwriting giving additional nisbas: al-ʿĪsī (from the house of ʿĪsā), al-Sharīf, al-Qurashī, al-Qaṣṣār. The author adds his own comment explaining al-ʿĪsī. Finally, it explains al-Tawḥīdī: attributed to the study of tawḥīd. This establishes al-Sanūsī's scholarly and spiritual pedigree.

Key Terms
السنوسي
التوحيدي
ترجمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'al-Tawḥīdī' is a sectarian label.
Correction: The text explicitly states it means 'engagement with the science of tawḥīd' (divine oneness), not a sect.

Checkpoint
What does the nisba 'al-Tawḥīdī' indicate about Imam al-Sanūsī?
A) He was from a tribe called Tawḥīd.
B) He was a theologian specializing in tawḥīd.
C) He wrote a book on tawḥīd.
D) He was a follower of the Tawḥīd sect.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi was a polymath theologian, and his nisba 'al-Tawhidi' underscores his specialization in the science of divine oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Imam al-Sanusi was a master in the science of tawhid. What attribute of Allah do you most struggle to truly internalize, and what concrete practice will you adopt this week to increase your certainty in it?
?
Imam al-Sanusi combined deep knowledge with piety (taqwa) and scrupulousness (wara'). Which area of your Islamic learning lacks the element of self-accountability—your prayer, your charity, or your speech? What is one specific action you will take today to bring that area into alignment with taqwa?
?
The passage mentions that his mother was a sharifa (descendant of the Prophet). If you are a follower of the Prophet, you are spiritually connected to him. How does that connection demand more from you in following the sunnah? Name one sunnah you have neglected and commit to reviving it starting tonight.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

The Dispute Over al-Sanusi's Birth Year
Dispute over al-Sanusi's birth year with two accounts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why there is disagreement over al-Sanusi's birth year and the two specific reports from his student al-Mallali.

Core Idea
Two conflicting accounts of al-Sanusi's age cause uncertainty about his birth year.

Biographical details of great scholars are sometimes unclear, and Imam al-Sanusi's birth year is a case in point. His biographers disagree because al-Sanusi himself never recorded his birth year, and his student al-Mallali gave contradictory reports. In this passage, we examine the two accounts and see why later scholars settled on a range.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the key terms and the flow of the narrative.
Pay attention to the two different ages mentioned (63 and 55).
2
Identify the two reports
Find the two reports from al-Mallali: one saying al-Sanusi died at 63, implying birth in 832 AH; another saying he was 55 about a year before death, implying birth in 840 AH.
Notice that both reports come from the same source, Nayl al-Ibtihaj.
3
Understand the scholarly response
Because of the inconsistency, later scholars like Ibn Maryam and al-Tanbuktī simply stated that his birth was after 830 AH, leaving the exact year ambiguous.
Also note the additional report from al-Balawi giving age 56 at death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مولده ونشأته. اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي ؛ وسبب ذلك يرجع لعدم نصه هو على ذلك ، واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً ، قال العلامة التنبكتي في نيل الابتهاج : ( رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء : أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ ، فقال له : مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة ). فعلى هذه الرواية : تكون السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام السنوسي هي ( ٨٣٢هـ ). وفي ( نيل الابتهاج ) أيضاً نقل قول الملالي : ( وأخبرني قبل موته بنحو عام أنَّ سنه خمس وخمسون سنة ) ، فتكون سنة ولادته على هذا ( ٨٤٠هـ ) ، والله أعلم ، ولهذا اكتفى ابن مريم والتنبكتي بقولهما : ( مولده بعد الثلاثين وثمان مئة ) ، وانظر ( البستان ) ( ص ٢٤٤ ) ، وعندما ذكر العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي خبر وفاته في « ثبته ) ( ص ٤٣٨ ) قال : ( وكانت سنه يومئذ ستاً وخمسين سنة ).
His birth and upbringing. There is disagreement regarding the year of the birth of Imam al-Sanūsī; the reason for that goes back to his not stating it himself, and the inconsistency of the transmission of his student al-Mallālī on that matter as well. Al-ʿAllāma al-Tanbuktī said in Nayl al-Ibtihāj: 'I saw it noted from some scholars that he asked the aforementioned al-Mallālī about the age of the shaykh, and he said to him: He died at sixty-three years of age.' So according to this narration, the year in which Imam al-Sanūsī was born is 832 AH. And in Nayl al-Ibtihāj also is transmitted the saying of al-Mallālī: 'He informed me about a year before his death that his age was fifty-five years,' so the year of his birth according to this is 840 AH. And God knows best. For this reason Ibn Maryam and al-Tanbuktī sufficed with saying: 'His birth was after thirty and eight hundred.' And see al-Bustān, p. 244. And when al-ʿAllāma Abū Jaʿfar al-Balawī mentioned the news of his death in his Thabat, p. 438, he said: 'His age that day was fifty-six years.'
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses the disagreement over Imam al-Sanūsī's birth year. It begins by noting the reason for the dispute: al-Sanūsī himself did not record his birth year, and his student al-Mallālī gave contradictory reports. The passage then presents two accounts from al-Tanbuktī's Nayl al-Ibtihāj: one that al-Sanūsī died at 63, implying a birth year of 832 AH, and another from al-Mallālī himself that he said his age was 55, implying a birth year of 840 AH. The passage also notes that due to this inconsistency, some scholars like Ibn Maryam and al-Tanbuktī only stated that his birth was after 830 AH. Finally, it cites al-Balawī's report that his age at death was 56, which would give yet another year. The passage presents the conflicting reports without resolving them, leaving the matter to God's knowledge.

Key Terms
مولده
اختلاف
الملالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the disagreement over al-Sanūsī's birth year means his historical record is unreliable or his scholarship is questionable.
Correction: Uncertainty about birth years is common for pre-modern scholars. It does not affect the reliability of their works or teachings. The passage shows that biographers honestly report the discrepancy without casting doubt on al-Sanūsī's stature.

Checkpoint
According to the first report in the passage, at what age did Imam al-Sanūsī die?
A) 55
B) 56
C) 63
D) 65

Key Takeaway
The disagreement over al-Sanūsī's birth year arises from conflicting reports from his student al-Mallālī, leading scholars to acknowledge the uncertainty rather than commit to a single year.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The companions and early scholars did not fuss over exact birth years, yet we spend time on such details. Is your pursuit of Islamic knowledge driven by a desire to draw closer to Allah, or by an academic curiosity that misses the spirit? Before today ends, pick one scholar whose life you will learn about with the intention of gaining iman, not just information.
?
Al-Sanūsī left his birth year unrecorded, trusting his reputation to Allah. Do you feel the need to document every detail of your life for others to appreciate you? Write down one thing you do purely for Allah's sake that you will never tell anyone about, and commit to keeping it hidden.
?
The scholars said 'Allahu a'lam' when they could not be certain. Are you quick to speak on matters you do not fully know? Today, intentionally refrain from giving an opinion on one Islamic issue until you have verified the source. If you are not sure, say 'Allahu a'lam' genuinely.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
Disagreement over al-Sanusi's Birth Year
Author discusses the disagreement on al-Sanusi's birth year and cites sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why scholars disagree about Imam al-Sanusi's birth year and how they handled the conflicting reports.

Core Idea
Conflicting student reports leave al-Sanusi's birth year uncertain.

Imam al-Sanusi, a great scholar, did not record his own birth year, and his student al-Mallali gave inconsistent statements. This passage shows how later biographers carefully documented these variations without forcing a single conclusion. You will see the primary sources they used and their cautious approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the content. Notice the different numbers mentioned.
The passage contains multiple dates and citations.
2
Identify the cause of disagreement
Look for the sentence explaining why scholars disagree. The author gives two reasons: al-Sanusi did not state his birth year, and his student al-Mallali transmitted inconsistent reports.
3
Examine the two main reports
Find the two reports from al-Mallali: one saying al-Sanusi died at 63 (birth 832 AH), another saying he was 55 a year before death (birth 840 AH).
These are from the same student but differ by about 8 years.
4
See the scholars' cautious conclusion
Notice that later scholars like Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti simply say 'after 830' to avoid speculating. The author also adds a third report from al-Balawi (age 56 at death).
This shows scholarly caution with uncertain historical data.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Think about why this uncertainty matters: it shows that even for great scholars, biographical details can be unclear, and scholars must transmit what they have without forcing certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي ؛ وسبب ذلك يرجع لعدم نصه على ذلك ، واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً ، قال العلامة التنبكتي في نيل الابتهاج (٢) : ( رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء : أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ ، فقال له : مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة ) فعلى هذه الرواية : تكون السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام السنوسي هي ( ٨٣٢هـ ) (١) تعريف الخلف برجال السلف ( ١ / ١٧٦ ) (٢) وقد لخص في هذا الكتاب سيرة الإمام السنوسي ، من كتاب « المواهب القدسية » لتلميذ الإمام السنوسي ؛ وهو الشيخ محمد بن عمر الملالي رحمه الله تعالى . . أحسن تلخيص (٣) نيل الابتهاج ( ص ٥٧٠ ) . (٤) وفي « نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٥٧٠ ) أيضاً نقل قول الملالي : ( وأخبرني قبل موته بنحو عام أنَّ سنه خمس وخمسون سنة ) ، فتكون سنة ولادته على هذا ( ٨٤٠هـ ) ، والله أعلم ، ولهذا اكتفى ابن مريم والتنبكتي بقولهما : ( مولده بعد الثلاثين وثمان مئة ) ، وانظر « البستان » ( ص ٢٤٤ ) ، وعندما ذكر العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي خبر وفاته في « ثبته » ( ص ٤٣٨ ) قال : ( وكانت سنه يومئذ ستاً وخمسين سنة )
There is disagreement about the year of the birth of Imam al-Sanusi; the reason for that goes back to his not stating it [himself], and the inconsistency of the transmission of his student al-Mallali in that as well. al-‛Allāma al-Tunbukti said in Nayl al-Ibtihāj (2): 'I saw a note from some scholars that he asked the aforementioned al-Mallali about the age of the Shaykh, and he said to him: He died at sixty-three years.' So according to this narration, the year in which Imam al-Sanusi was born is 832 AH. (1) Ta‛rīf al-Khalaf bi-Rijāl al-Salaf (1/176). (2) He summarized in this book the biography of Imam al-Sanusi from the book 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' by the student of Imam al-Sanusi, Shaykh Muḥammad ibn ‛Umar al-Mallali, may Allah have mercy on him, a good summary. (3) Nayl al-Ibtihāj (p. 570). (4) Also in 'Nayl al-Ibtihāj' (p. 570) is transmitted the saying of al-Mallali: 'He informed me about a year before his death that his age was fifty-five years.' So the year of his birth according to this would be 840 AH. And Allah knows best. For this reason, Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti sufficed with their saying: 'His birth was after 830.' And see 'al-Bustān' (p. 244). And when al-‛Allāma Abū Ja‛far al-Balawī mentioned news of his death in his 'Thabat' (p. 438), he said: 'His age on that day was fifty-six years.'
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage deals with the uncertainty surrounding the birth year of Imam al-Sanusi. The author states that the disagreement arises because al-Sanusi himself did not specify his birth year, and his student al-Mallali transmitted inconsistent reports. The author then presents two narrations from al-Mallali via secondary sources. First, he cites al-Tunbukti who recorded that al-Mallali said the Shaykh died at age 63, which would place his birth in 832 AH. Second, in footnote (4), he gives another report from al-Mallali stating that al-Sanusi was 55 years old about a year before his death, implying a birth year of 840 AH. The author notes that some later scholars like Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti simply say his birth was after 830 AH to avoid speculating. Finally, he adds a third piece of evidence from al-Balawi, who said al-Sanusi was 56 at death, which would correspond to yet another possible year. The passage shows the careful documentation of conflicting historical reports without forcing a single conclusion.

Key Terms
الخلاف
سنة الولادة
الملالي
نيل الابتهاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Sanusi's birth year is definitively known and recorded without dispute.
Correction: The passage shows that even his student gave conflicting reports, leading later scholars to state only a general period (after 830) rather than a specific year.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there disagreement about al-Sanusi's birth year?
A) Because his father forgot the year
B) Because al-Sanusi did not state his birth year and his student al-Mallali gave inconsistent reports
C) Because the historians all agree but the footnotes are unreliable
D) Because the year 832 AH is the only one mentioned

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's birth year remains uncertain because his own student transmitted conflicting ages, leading scholars to adopt a cautious approach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even the direct student of a renowned scholar like Imam al-Sanusi transmitted inconsistent information about his teacher's age, how much more careful must we be when speaking about matters of faith? What is one thing you have been repeating without verification, and what will you do to check it?
?
The scholars refrained from giving a definitive birth year when the evidence was inconclusive, saying only 'after 830'. In your own life, are there beliefs or practices you hold with certainty that actually rest on shaky evidence? Will you have the humility to say 'Allah knows best' and remain open to correction?
?
The contradictions in al-Mallali's reports did not lead the scholars to discard all his narrations; they preserved them honestly. When you encounter disagreements among trusted sources, do you become anxious or dismissive? How can you adopt the balanced approach of acknowledging uncertainty without abandoning trust in the tradition?

Al-Sanusi's Upbringing and Father's Virtues
Author describes al-Sanusi's noble lineage, upbringing in Tlemcen, and his father's piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pious and scholarly environment in which Imam al-Sanusi was raised, the character of his father Yūsuf Abū Ya‛qūb, and the significance of his Hasanid lineage.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's piety was nurtured by a righteous father and a blessed environment.

This passage introduces the early life of Imam al-Sanusi, showing how his upbringing in a household of virtue and learning shaped his future. We see his father's description, the spiritual atmosphere of Tlemcen, and his noble lineage. Let's read the source to appreciate the foundations of his scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the biographical details come through.
Notice the description of his father.
2
Identify the father's virtues
From the passage, list the qualities attributed to al-Sanusi's father by al-Mallali. Consider how these virtues influenced al-Sanusi.
The father is described as righteous, ascetic, humble, devout, etc.
3
Consider the lineage detail
Note that al-Sanusi's paternal grandmother was of Hasanid descent, giving him the epithet al-Hasanī. Reflect on the importance of noble lineage in Islamic scholarship.
4
Reflect on the father's occupation and miracles
The father taught Qur’an to children and was blessed with miracles and spiritual insight. Think about how this humble occupation reflects his piety.
Al-Mallali mentions divine care and unveiling of insight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم ؛ فوالده هو الشيخ الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب (۱) ، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم ، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها ، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين . وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنية النسب ، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه (٢) . وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام : ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه . . رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً ، خاشعاً الله تعالى ، زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها ، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى ، سالم الصدر ، حسن الأخلاق ، مبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه ، حسن المعاشرة ، كريم الطبع ) (٣) . وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب ، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أنَّ عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته ، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته . (۱) انظر « المواهب القدسية » ( ق ) . (٢) انظر « المواهب القدسية » ( ق ) . (٣) انظر « المواهب القدسية » ( ق )
Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a house of virtue and knowledge. His father was the righteous, ascetic, humble, investigating master Yūsuf Abū Ya‛qūb (1), and from him the Imam took the principles of the sciences, and that was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge in its day, and the clay of saints and righteous ones. The grandmother of Imam al-Sanusi on his father's side was of Hasanid lineage, therefore the Imam was sometimes called al-Hasanī through his paternal grandmother (2). al-Shaykh al-Mallali said in describing the Imam's father: 'My master Yūsuf al-Sanūsī, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son... was a righteous, devout man, humble before Allah, ascetic in this world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to Allah, sound of heart, good of character, smiling in the face of everyone he met, good in companionship, generous of nature' (3). The craft of this blessed father was teaching the Qur’an to children in the school (maktab). It appears from the words of al-Mallali that divine care accompanied him from his childhood, so Allah worked miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight. (1) See 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' (folio). (2) See 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' (folio). (3) See 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' (folio).
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage provides biographical information about Imam al-Sanusi's early life. It first states that he grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge, highlighting the influence of his father, Yūsuf Abū Ya‛qūb, who is described as a righteous, ascetic, and learned teacher. The author notes that al-Sanusi learned the basics of the sciences from his father in Tlemcen, which was then a center of learning. Then, a detail about lineage: his paternal grandmother was a Sharīfa (descendant of al-Hasan), which explains why al-Sanusi was sometimes called al-Hasanī. The author then quotes al-Mallali's description of the father, emphasizing his piety, asceticism, and good character. Finally, it mentions that the father's occupation was teaching the Qur’an to children, and that he was blessed with miraculous occurrences and spiritual insight from an early age, as per al-Mallali's account. The footnotes refer to the source manuscript 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' by al-Mallali.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume al-Sanusi's father was a famous scholar or jurist, but he was a modest Qur’an teacher, though highly pious.
Correction: The passage shows his father was a righteous and devout Qur’an teacher, not a renowned scholar, but his piety and spiritual state were exemplary.

Checkpoint
Why was Imam al-Sanusi sometimes called al-Hasanī?
A) Because his father was named Hasan
B) Because his paternal grandmother was of Hasanid lineage
C) Because he was born in the city of Hasan
D) Because his teacher al-Mallali gave him that title

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's upbringing in a household of virtue and knowledge, with a pious father and noble lineage, laid the foundation for his later scholarship and spirituality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your family environment: Is your home a 'house of virtue and knowledge' like that of Imam al-Sanusi? What concrete steps can you take this week to emulate the pious atmosphere described in this passage, even if you feel your circumstances fall short?
?
Al-Sanusi's father was a humble Qur'an teacher, not a famous scholar, yet he raised a great imam. What does this teach you about the true measure of a parent's legacy? Are you seeking worldly recognition in your own role—whether as a parent, teacher, or community member—or are you content with sincere, hidden service?
?
The passage mentions that the father's soul was 'sound of heart' and 'smiling in the face of everyone he met'. How often do you greet others with a genuine smile reflecting inner contentment with Allah? What negative emotions or attachments are robbing you of that soundness of heart, and what will you do to remove them this week?

Al-Sanusi's Teachers and Spiritual Care
Author states al-Sanusi's dual formation through scholars and saints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of spiritual blessing (baraka) through the glances of saints in al-Sanusi's educational journey.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's education combined scholarly study with divine care.

This lesson introduces the brief but profound statement that al-Sanusi studied under the top scholars of his time and also received special spiritual attention from saints. This dual aspect — academic erudition and spiritual blessing — is a hallmark of traditional Islamic learning. The passage reminds us that in Islamic tradition, knowledge is not merely intellectual but also infused with divine grace.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two sources of al-Sanusi's formation: scholars and saints.
The footnote references a manuscript source.
2
Understand key terms
Focus on the terms 'jillat al-'ulamā' (leading scholars) and 'lahaẓāt al-awliyā' (glances of saints). What do they imply?
'Lahaẓāt' is a spiritual concept, not physical.
3
Reflect on the dual aspect
Consider why mentioning spiritual care alongside scholarly study is important in Islamic biography. It shows that true knowledge is blessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيوخه : أخذ الإمام السنوسي العلم عن جلة علماء عصره ، ونالته عناية ولحظات الأولياء والصالحين . (۱) انظر « المواهب القدسية » ( ق )
His teachers: Imam al-Sanusi acquired knowledge from the leading scholars of his time, and attained divine care and glances of the saints and righteous ones. (1) See 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' (folio).
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This very brief passage introduces the section on al-Sanusi's teachers. It states that he studied under the eminent scholars of his era, and that he received divine attention and the spiritual glances (lahaẓāt) of the saints and righteous individuals. The term 'lahaẓāt' implies that the awliya’ looked upon him with favor, which is considered a source of blessing. The footnote again references the manuscript of al-Mallali as the source. This passage is a general statement before the author presumably lists specific teachers (though the OCR ends here).

Key Terms

عناية
لحظات الأولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'glances of saints' are literal physical looks.
Correction: In this context, 'lahaẓāt' metaphorically refers to spiritual favor and attention from the saints, not physical glances.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what else did al-Sanusi attain besides knowledge from scholars?
A) Wealth and fame
B) Divine care and the glances of saints
C) A position as a judge
D) The ability to perform miracles

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi's education was enriched by both scholarly excellence and the spiritual blessings of saints.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own pursuit of knowledge, do you actively seek the duas and spiritual support of pious individuals, or do you rely solely on academic study? What might you be missing?
?
The 'glances of saints' are described as a source of divine favor. Have you ever experienced or sought such spiritual attention? Why or why not?
?
If you had to choose between studying under a great scholar or having the care of a saint, which would you prioritize? Does this lesson challenge that assumption?

Imam al-Sanusi's Noble Lineage and Early Education
Describes al-Sanusi's noble family, father's piety, and early education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the family background and spiritual environment that shaped Imam al-Sanusi's education and character.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's lineage and upbringing were the foundation of his scholarly and spiritual authority.

Imam al-Sanusi did not emerge from a vacuum. His family, his father's piety, and the city of Tlemcen all contributed to his formation. This passage introduces the roots of his knowledge and baraka.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the emphasis on lineage and the description of his father.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بيت فضل وعلم' – household of virtue and knowledge.
2
Reflect on the father's description
Consider the qualities of Imam al-Sanusi's father as described by Shaykh al-Mallali. What do these qualities suggest about the environment in which al-Sanusi grew up?
His father was not only a scholar but also an ascetic and a saintly figure.
3
Consider the spiritual dimension
The passage mentions divine care and miracles from childhood. How does this frame al-Sanusi's own spiritual and scholarly standing?
The biography establishes al-Sanusi as inheriting both knowledge and spiritual grace.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم ؛ فوالده هو الشيخ الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم ، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها ، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين. وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنية النسب، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه. وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام : ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه . . رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً ، خاشعاً الله تعالى ، زاهداً في الدنيا معرضاً عنها ، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى ، سالم الصدر ، حسن الأخلاق ، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه ، حسن المعاشرة ، كريم الطبع ). وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب ، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أنَّ عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته ، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته. شيوه أخذ الإمام السنوسي العلم عن جلة علماء عصره ، ونالته عناية ولحظات الأولياء والصالحين.
Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge; his father was the righteous, ascetic, humble teacher, the investigator Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, and from him the Imam took the principles of sciences, and that was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge in its day, and the clay of saints and righteous ones. And the grandmother of Imam al-Sanusi on his father's side was of Hasani lineage, and therefore the Imam may be called al-Hasani from his paternal grandmother's side. And Shaykh al-Mallali said in describing the Imam's father: 'Sayyidi Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah Most High have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son... a righteous, pious man, humble before Allah Most High, ascetic in this world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to Allah Most High, pure of heart, good of character, smiling in the face of everyone he met, good in companionship, noble in nature.' And the profession of this blessed father was teaching the Qur'an to children in the school. And it appears from the words of Shaykh al-Mallali that Allah's care accompanied him from his childhood, and Allah caused miracles to happen at his hands and unveiled his insight. His teachers: Imam al-Sanusi took knowledge from the foremost scholars of his time, and he received the care and glances of the saints and righteous ones.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Sanusi. It first establishes his lineage, stating that he grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge. His father, Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, is described as a righteous and ascetic teacher, and from him al-Sanusi learned the foundations of knowledge. The location is Tlemcen, then a center of learning. Next, it mentions his grandmother on his father's side was a Hasani sharifa, which gives al-Sanusi a lineage linked to the Prophet Muhammad. The passage then quotes Shaykh al-Mallali's description of al-Sanusi's father, emphasizing his piety and character. Finally, it notes that the father's profession was teaching the Qur'an to children, and that divine care accompanied al-Sanusi from childhood, with miracles attributed to his father. The passage concludes by stating that al-Sanusi learned from the eminent scholars of his era and received spiritual care from saints.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's upbringing in a household of virtue and knowledge, with a father who was both a scholar and a saint, set the stage for his future achievements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage describes Tlemcen as 'the clay of saints and righteous ones'. Your environment matters. What is one thing in your current environment (home, workplace, social circle) that is pulling you away from righteousness, and what step will you take to distance yourself from it within the next 48 hours?

Al-Sanusi's Study of the Seven Qira'at
Details al-Sanusi's expertise in Quranic recitations and his teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rigorous process by which Imam al-Sanusi mastered the seven Quranic recitations and the chain of his teachers.

Core Idea
Mastery of qira'at required multiple complete recitations and licenses from renowned teachers.

This passage from al-Balawi's account highlights al-Sanusi's exceptional dedication to the science of qira'at. It details his study under three major teachers, each involving complete recitations of the Quran and receiving ijazas. Understanding this process gives insight into the traditional Islamic educational system and al-Sanusi's scholarly credentials.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Get a sense of the overall account of al-Sanusi's qira'at studies.
Pay attention to the names and the technical terms.
2
Identify the three teachers
From the passage, list the three main teachers: Abu al-Hajjaj, al-Yaznasni, and al-Laja'i. Note what each taught and how many recitations (khatma) were involved.
Teacher 1: Abu al-Hajjaj – two complete recitations plus a portion of a third. Teacher 2: al-Yaznasni – one complete recitation plus three hizbs. Teacher 3: al-Laja'i – partial recitation (Fatiha, Baqara, first of Al Imran).
3
Understand the concept of ijaza
Notice that each teacher granted al-Sanusi an ijaza (license) to teach and transmit. This is a key feature of traditional Islamic education.
An ijaza is a certification of competence and permission to transmit.
4
Trace the chain of transmission
The passage ends with the chain back to two earlier teachers: Abu Abdullah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut. This shows the continuity of the oral tradition.

وكان للإمام السنوسي علو كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءة على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة « البقرة » ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي ، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما )
And Imam al-Sanusi was highly skilled in collecting the recitations; for the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven recitations from the jurist, teacher, scholar, practitioner, investigator, reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf bin al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-Abbas Ahmad bin Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: And I added from a third a good portion whose extent I have not now verified, collecting the seven according to the contents of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he (the teacher) gave him a general absolute license in the seven recitations and in other things from his narrations. And he (al-Balawi) narrated to him the seven from the two imams, scholars, teachers: the noble, most knowledgeable, most famous, reciter, investigator, [؟], humble teacher Abu al-Abbas Ahmad bin Abi 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasni, and the noble, glorified, famous, investigator, precise, meticulous, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, pure teacher Abu al-Abbas Ahmad bin al-Faqih, the versatile scholar Abu Abdullah Muhammad bin 'Isa al-Laja'i. He read to the first as a collective recitation in one complete recitation of the seven; he said: And I added three parts from Surat al-Baqara. And to the second he read al-Fatiha, al-Baqara, and the beginnings of Al 'Imran as a collective recitation of the seven; and he received a license for what he read and what remained. They both narrated to him together that from the two teachers: Abu Abdullah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut by their chains.)
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a testimony to Imam al-Sanusi's expertise in the science of qira'at (Quranic recitations). It quotes al-Balawi, who states that al-Sanusi studied the seven canonical readings under Abu al-Hajjaj al-Hasani. Al-Sanusi recited two complete khatmat (recitations of the entire Quran) to him and added a portion of a third, using the texts of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya as his basis. He received a general ijaza (license) from this teacher. Next, al-Balawi lists two other teachers from whom al-Sanusi learned the seven recitations: al-Yaznasni and al-Laja'i. With al-Yaznasni, he performed one complete khatma and added three hizbs from Surat al-Baqara. With al-Laja'i, he recited from al-Fatiha, al-Baqara, and the beginning of Al 'Imran, also as a collective reading. He received ijaza from both. The chain continues back to two earlier teachers: Abu Abdullah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut. The passage demonstrates the rigor and thoroughness of al-Sanusi's traditional education in qira'at.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The seven recitations refer to different Qur'ans.
Correction: The seven recitations (qira'at) are accepted variant readings of the same Quran, not different texts.

Checkpoint
How many complete recitations (khatmat) did al-Sanusi study with Abu al-Hajjaj?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi's mastery of qira'at was achieved through multiple intensive oral recitations and formal ijazas from leading scholars, reflecting the rigor of traditional Islamic education.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Sanusi dedicated multiple complete recitations to each teacher. When was the last time you recited an entire Quran from memory to a qualified teacher? If never, what is stopping you from seeking that connection to the oral tradition?
?
He studied under three different scholars for just one subject (qira'at). In your own pursuit of Islamic knowledge, have you prioritized breadth across topics or depth with multiple teachers in a single science? Which approach does your current situation demand from you right now?
?
The ijaza al-Sanusi received connects him to the Prophet ﷺ through an unbroken chain. Does the reality of that chain make any difference to how you value the Quran you recite daily? If so, how will you change your recitation habits starting today?

Al-Sanusi's Mastery of the Seven Qira'at
Al-Balawi narrates Sanusi's chains of transmission in qira'at.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth and authenticity of al-Sanusi's training in the seven qira'at through multiple chains of transmission.

Core Idea
Sanusi's qira'a mastery rested on multiple, verified chains of transmission.

This lesson presents a biographical account of al-Sanusi's expertise in the science of qira'at, as narrated by the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi. The passage details the teachers from whom Sanusi learned, the specific recitations he performed, and the ijazas he received. By examining these chains, we gain insight into the rigorous traditional educational system and the high caliber of Sanusi's scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage attentively
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the names and the structure of the transmission chains.
The passage includes a direct quotation from al-Balawi.
2
Identify the main teachers
List the three teachers mentioned: Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf, Abu al-'Abbas al-Yaznasni, and Abu al-'Abbas al-Laja'i. Note how Sanusi studied with each.
Each teacher had a different method of instruction.
3
Understand the modes of transmission
Notice the terms: 'khatma' (complete recitation), 'ijaza' (authorization), and 'riwaya' (narration). See how Sanusi received both oral recitation and written authorization.
The combination of multiple modes strengthens authenticity.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why al-Balawi recorded these details. They demonstrate Sanusi's thorough training and the interconnectedness of scholarly chains.
This passage highlights the importance of isnad in Islamic sciences.

وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ; فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين , قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة , وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني , والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي , قراءة على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة , قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة « البقرة » , وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع , وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي , حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي , وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما )
And al-Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the collection of the qira'at. For the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven qira'at from the jurist, teacher, scholar, worker, verified, reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting upon him in two complete recitations. He said: And I added from the third a sufficient amount whose extent I have not now ascertained, collecting the seven according to the content of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he gave him a general absolute ijaza in the seven recitations and in other things he transmitted. And he narrated the seven to him from the two great, teaching imams: the noble, most knowledgeable, most famous, verified reciter, humble, devoted master Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasni, and the noble, revered, famous, verified, precise, proficient, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, pure master Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn al-faqih, scholar, versatile Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Laja'i. He read upon the first in a combined complete recitation for the seven. He said: And I added three parts from Surah al-Baqarah. And upon the second for the Opening of the Book, al-Baqarah, and the beginnings of Al 'Imran, combined for the seven. And an ijaza for what he read and what remained. They both narrated it from the two masters: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhut, with their chain.'
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of al-Sanusi's mastery in the science of qira'at, quoting the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi. It first asserts that al-Sanusi had high standing ('uluww ka'ib) in collecting the qira'at. Then al-Balawi narrates that al-Sanusi took the seven qira'at from Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations (khatmatayn). Al-Balawi adds that he himself (al-Balawi) added a sufficient amount from a third recitation, collecting the seven according to the famous works al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. Al-Sanusi received a general absolute ijaza from him. Al-Balawi also narrates that al-Sanusi heard the seven from two other master reciters: Abu al-'Abbas al-Yaznasni and Abu al-'Abbas al-Laja'i. Details are given: with al-Yaznasni he read a combined khatma for the seven, adding three ajza' from Surat al-Baqarah; with al-Laja'i he read selected parts (al-Fatiha, al-Baqarah, and beginnings of Al 'Imran) combined for the seven, and received ijaza for what he read and what remained. Both masters transmitted from Abu 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhut. The passage emphasizes the breadth and authenticity of Sanusi's qira'a training.

?
Sanusi added extra portions beyond the required readings, showing a desire for depth. Are you content with just 'completing the basics' in your religious studies, or do you push yourself to go deeper? Identify one topic where you can commit to extra effort beyond the minimum.

Al-Sanusi's Diverse Teachers and Sciences
Lists Sanusi's teachers in fiqh, usul, hadith, astronomy, and more.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wide range of Islamic sciences that al-Sanusi studied under various renowned scholars, from qira'at to astronomy.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi mastered both transmitted and rational sciences through a diverse network of teachers.

This passage offers a glimpse into the traditional Islamic education system, where students traveled and studied under multiple specialists. Al-Sanusi's teachers represent expertise in Qur'anic recitation, law, theology, logic, rhetoric, astronomy, inheritance, and mathematics, showing his comprehensive training. As you read the passage, notice how each teacher is associated with a specific science or set of sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing every name. Then read the translation. Focus on the variety of subjects mentioned.
The passage is a list of teachers and what they taught.
2
Identify the teachers and their specializations
Go through each teacher mentioned and note the science or sciences they taught al-Sanusi. Use the translation to help.
For example, al-Maghili taught fiqh; al-Tilmisani taught usul, mantiq, bayan, and fiqh.
3
Notice the transmission methods
Observe terms like 'aqadhu' (took from), 'qara'a' (read upon), 'rawa' (narrated), and 'ajaza' (gave ijaza). These indicate different ways of learning and authorization.
Ijaza and samaa' (hearing) are key concepts in hadith transmission.
4
Reflect on the breadth of education
Consider how al-Sanusi studied both transmitted sciences (qira'at, hadith) and rational sciences (logic, astronomy). What does this tell you about his scholarly profile?
This breadth was common among major scholars of his time.

ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر الزواوي , والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي والشيخ الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني , أخذ عنه القراءات السبع , والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب , أخذ عنه الفقه , والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب , والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني , قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه , والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه , قرأ عليه ( الرسالة ) , وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ( الإرشاد ) لإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي , فروى عنه ( الصحيحين ) وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر , وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه , وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي , وأجازه بجميع ما يروي , كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد
And among the scholars upon whom he read: Shaykh, scholar Nasr al-Zawawi, and Shaykh, scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sinhaji, and Shaykh al-Sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani - he took from him the seven qira'at. And Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab - he took from him fiqh. And the scholar, mu'addil Abu 'Abd Allah al-Habak - he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-Tilmisani - he read upon him usul, mantiq, bayan, and fiqh. And the hafiz Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother - he read upon him al-Risala. And he and this brother read upon the pious, righteous Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi al-Irshad of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid. And he occupied himself with narration and sciences of athar upon the pious, righteous Imam Abu Zayd 'Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi. So he narrated from him al-Sahihayn and other books of hadith and athar, and he gave him ijaza for what he was permitted and from him, and made him hear the musalsalat and others. And he read fara'id and hisab upon the noble scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalsadi al-Andalusi, and he gave him ijaza in all he narrated. Also, Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif gave him ijaza from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage enumerates the many teachers of al-Sanusi across various Islamic sciences. It lists scholars he studied under, starting with Nasr al-Zawawi and Muhammad ibn Tumart (both for qira'at), and Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf (again for qira'at). Then it mentions Abu 'Abd Allah al-Maghili for fiqh, Abu 'Abd Allah al-Habak for astronomy ('ilm al-asṭurlāb), and Imam Muhammad al-Tilmisani for uṣūl, manṭiq, bayān, and fiqh. His maternal brother al-Hasan al-Taluti taught him al-Risāla (likely of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani). Together with his brother, he studied al-Irshād of al-Juwayni and 'ilm al-tawḥīd under al-Kanabishi. For hadith and athar, he studied with al-Tha'alibi, narrating al-Ṣaḥīḥayn and other works, receiving ijaza and hearing musalsalāt. Finally, for farā'id and ḥisāb, he studied with al-Qalsadi, and also received ijaza from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif through his father. The list demonstrates the breadth of Sanusi's education across transmitted and rational sciences.

?

?

How does his example challenge that fear? What step can you take this week to engage with a rational science through an Islamic lens?

Al-Zawawi, and the scholar, the world, Muhammad bin Tumart al-Sanhaji. (1) 6 And the noble master Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf bin Abi al-Abbas Ahmad bin Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, he took from him the seven Qur'anic readings. And the master Abu Abdullah Muhammad bin Ahmad bin Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab, he took from him fiqh. And the just scholar Abu Abdullah al-Habbak, he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And the Imam Muhammad bin al-Abbas al-Tilimsani, he read upon him usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh. And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali bin Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother, he read upon him 'al-Risala', and he and his brother read upon the pious, righteous Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi 'al-Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid. And he occupied himself with narration and the sciences of hadith upon the pious, righteous Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, so he narrated from him the two Sahihs and other books of hadith and athar, and he authorized him with what is permissible for him and from him, and he heard from him the musalsalat and others. And he read inheritance calculation and arithmetic upon the eminent scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he authorized him with all that he narrates, and similarly authorized him Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid (2). (1) And it is said: 'Tuzat' instead of 'Tumart', and he is not Ibn Tumart, the Mahdi of the Almohads, as is not hidden. (2) Mentioned that the scholar Muhammad Makhlu in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387).
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of Imam al-Sanusi's teachers and the subjects he studied with each. It begins by naming al-Zawawi and Muhammad bin Tumart al-Sanhaji, with a footnote clarifying that this Ibn Tumart is not the famous Almohad Mahdi. Then it lists: 1) Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Sharif al-Hasani, from whom he studied the seven Qur'anic readings. 2) Abu Abdullah al-Maghili (al-Jallab), for fiqh. 3) Abu Abdullah al-Habbak, for the science of the astrolabe. 4) Muhammad bin al-Abbas al-Tilimsani, for usul (foundations of jurisprudence), logic, rhetoric (bayan), and fiqh. 5) Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti, his maternal brother, for the Risala of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani. Then both Sanusi and his brother studied with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi, from whom they studied al-Juwayni's 'al-Irshad' and the science of tawhid. Next, Sanusi occupied himself with hadith narration and transmission (athar) under Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the Sahihs and other hadith works, received ijaza, and heard musalsal hadiths. Finally, he studied inheritance and arithmetic under Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who also authorized him. Another ijaza came from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif via his father. The passage demonstrates the breadth of Sanusi’s early education, encompassing both transmitted (Qur'an, hadith, fiqh) and rational (logic, rhetoric, astronomy) sciences.

Al-Sanusi's Teachers: A Diverse Network of Scholars
Al-Balawi lists al-Sanusi's teachers, including local scholars and specialists in various fields.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of al-Sanusi's scholarly network as reflected in the list of his teachers.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's education reflects the interconnectedness of Islamic scholarship.

This passage continues al-Sanusi's biography, listing the various teachers from whom he studied. These names reveal not only his teachers but also the type of knowledge he acquired—from jurisprudence to calculation and inheritance. Let's explore this rich scholarly chain.

أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ « أبركان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه عن الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) .
Al-Alama al-Balawi said: 'He took from the teachers of his town from a group of our teachers and others, and among their greatest: the friend of Allah, the Imam, the world, the righteous Abu Ali al-Ahsan, known as Abarkan, and Imam Abu Abdullah bin al-Abbas – but he did not take much from him – and others. And he also took from our master Abu Abdullah bin Marzuq, and our master Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the branch jurist Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the eminent jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabili, author of the versification of al-Mukhtasar – I think he took from him – and he took the science of calculation and inheritance from the distinguished jurist in them, Abu Abdullah bin Tumart, and also took from his brother mentioned earlier. Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the biographical listing of al-Sanusi's teachers, quoted from al-Alama al-Balawi. It mentions: 1) Abu Ali al-Ahsan (known as Abarkan), described as a saint and righteous scholar. 2) Abu Abdullah bin al-Abbas, though al-Sanusi did not take much from him. 3) Abu Abdullah bin Marzuq. 4) Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi. 5) Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, a branch jurist. 6) Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabili, who versified al-Mukhtasar. 7) Abu Abdullah bin Tumart, from whom he learned inheritance and calculation. 8) The brother of the latter, already mentioned. The passage also notes that al-Sanusi's student, Abu Abdullah Muhammad bin Umar al-Mallali, compiled a book introducing him, which includes these teachers. The variety of teachers shows al-Sanusi's broad network and the communal nature of Islamic scholarship.

Al-Sanusi's Sufi Training and Spiritual Influence
Discusses the Sufi influence on al-Sanusi, especially from Ibrahim al-Tazi, and his ijaza practices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Sufi influences on al-Sanusi, particularly the role of Ibrahim al-Tazi, and the significance of his thabat in preserving spiritual chains.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's spirituality was rooted in a living chain of transmission through his master Ibrahim al-Tazi.

Al-Sanusi is known as a theologian, but his spiritual formation was deeply rooted in Sufi training. This passage reveals the figures who shaped his inner life, especially the saintly Ibrahim al-Tazi, and shows how he preserved the chains of Sufi practices through a small thabat. Let's examine the details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key spiritual influence
Read the Arabic text and translation to find who had the greatest impact on al-Sanusi's spiritual training. Look for the phrase 'كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر'.
The name is Ibrahim bin Muhammad bin Ali al-Tazi.
2
Understand the ijaza system
Notice that al-Sanusi narrated by general ijaza from several scholars. Consider how this broad permission coexists with specific chains in his thabat.
General ijaza does not negate specific chains; both are used.
3
Examine the thabat contents
List the seven practices mentioned in the thabat. They include hadiths and Sufi practices like wearing the khirqa and teaching dhikr.
Each item has a chain going back to Ibrahim al-Tazi.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصوف وتربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي ظهر أنّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي
نزيل وهران. كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من
هذا
وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ( فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٢/ ٩٩٩ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي )
Sufism and his moral training. There are great gnostic figures that influenced Imam al-Sanusi, but what appeared is that the saintly, gnostic, righteous master Ibrahim bin Muhammad bin Ali al-Tazi, resident of Wahran, was the one with the greatest influence on Imam al-Sanusi in this regard. And al-Alama al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fihras al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: 'And he has a small thabat in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of primacy, the hadith of hospitality upon the two black things, the handshake, the interlocking, wearing the khirqa, handing the misbaha, and the teaching of dhikr by way of his master Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.'
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a distinct section on al-Sanusi's Sufi and moral training. It first states that there were many great gnostic figures who influenced him, but the one with the greatest impact was Ibrahim bin Muhammad bin Ali al-Tazi, a resident of Oran. Then it quotes al-Kattani's 'Fihras al-Faharis', noting that al-Sanusi narrated by general ijaza from al-Tha'alibi, al-Qalasadi, etc. More specifically, al-Sanusi had a small thabat (a record of chains of transmission) that contained the chains for several Sufi practices: hadith of primacy, hospitality on the two black things, handshake, interlocking fingers, wearing the khirqa (Sufi cloak), handing the misbaha (prayer beads), and instruction in dhikr – all transmitted from his master Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi. This shows that al-Sanusi's spirituality was rooted in a living chain of transmission through his Sufi shaykh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: General ijaza means no need for specific chains.
Correction: General ijaza is a broad permission, but specific chains for practices are still preserved, as seen in al-Sanusi's thabat.

Teachers of Imam Sanusi as Listed by al-Balawi and al-Kattani
Al-Balawi and al-Kattani list the teachers and ijazah sources of Imam Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Imam Sanusi's teachers across disciplines and regions, as documented by al-Balawi and al-Kattani.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi studied under a wide network of scholars across North Africa.

This passage takes us into the biographical tradition that records the teachers of Imam Sanusi. Al-Balawi provides a detailed list of names, highlighting Sanusi's diverse studies from fiqh to arithmetic. Al-Kattani adds a note on his ijazah chain through al-Tazi. Together, they show the scholarly authority behind Sanusi's own work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from al-Balawi and al-Kattani.
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview of the names and subjects mentioned.
2
Identify the different teachers and their specialties.
Notice that al-Balawi groups teachers by town and subject. Al-Kattani focuses on ijazah.
3
Reflect on the significance of this list.
Consider how this teacher network contributed to Sanusi's authority in kalam and other sciences.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ « أبركان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه عن الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) .
وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ( فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٢/ ٩٩٩ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي ) .
Al-ʿAllāmah al-Balawī said: "He (Imam al-Sanūsī) took from the scholars of his town from a group of our teachers and others, and among their greatest: the friend of Allah, the imam, the scholar, the righteous Abū ʿAlī al-Aḥsan known as 'Abarkan', and the Imam Abū ʿAbdillāh ibn al-ʿAbbās—though he did not take much from him—and others. He also took from our teacher Abū ʿAbdillāh ibn Marzūq, our teacher Abū al-Ḥasan al-Qalṣādī, the jurist of branches Abū ʿAbdillāh al-Jallāb, and the eminent jurist Abū al-Faraj al-Ghirāblī, author of the versification of al-Mukhtaṣar; I think he took from him. He learned arithmetic and inheritance law from the jurist distinguished in them Abū ʿAbdillāh ibn Tūmart, and he also took from his brother mentioned earlier. And among those whom his student, our companion the jurist, the noble, the accomplished, the blessed Abū ʿAbdillāh Muḥammad ibn ʿUmar al-Mallālī included in the book 'al-Taʿrīf bihi'."
And al-ʿAllāmah al-Kattānī mentioned in 'Fihris al-Fahāris' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanūsī narrated by general authorization (ijāzah) from Abū Zayd ʿAbd al-Raḥmān al-Thaʿālibī, Abū al-Ḥasan al-Qalṣādī, and others. He said: "He has a small register (thabat) in which he mentioned the chain of the ḥadīth of al-Awwaliyyah, the ḥadīth of hospitality upon the two black things, the handshake, interlocking fingers, wearing the patched cloak, handing over the prayer beads, and instilling the dhikr through the path of his teacher Abū Isḥāq Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī."
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section that lists the teachers of Imam Sanusi. It begins with a quote from al-Balawi, who enumerates the scholars from whom Sanusi studied. He first mentions the scholars from Sanusi's own town, including the friend of Allah, Imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as Abarkan, and Imam Abu Abdillah ibn al-Abbas, though Sanusi did not take much from the latter. Then al-Balawi lists other teachers: Abu Abdillah ibn Marzuq, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalsadi, the jurist Abu Abdillah al-Jallab, and the eminent jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Ghirabli, author of a versification of al-Mukhtasar. He notes that Sanusi also studied arithmetic and inheritance law from Abu Abdillah ibn Tumart, and from the latter's brother. These teachers were all included by Sanusi's student al-Mallali in his biographical work. Then the passage adds a note from al-Kattani, who states that Sanusi transmitted by general ijazah from Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalsadi, and others. Al-Kattani mentions a small thabat (register) in which Sanusi recorded the chains for several hadiths and practices, all through his teacher Ibrahim al-Tazi. This highlights the breadth of Sanusi's learning and the authority of his transmission.
