The Spiritual Influence of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi on Imam Sanusi
Biographical description of Ibrahim al-Tazi's influence on Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi's spiritual and moral example shaped Imam Sanusi's path, and recognize the qualities that made al-Tazi a revered saint and teacher.

Core Idea
Ibrahim al-Tazi's patience and virtue became legendary, and his spiritual influence was the greatest on Sanusi.

This passage from Sanusi's biographical tradition highlights the profound impact of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi on his spiritual formation. While Sanusi studied under many scholars, it was al-Tazi's combination of deep knowledge and saintly character that left the deepest mark. The text paints a vivid picture of a man whose intellect, forbearance, and devotion became proverbial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of al-Tazi's qualities.
Notice the structure: first the claim of greatest influence, then al-Tazi's attributes, then the quotation about his proverbial status.
2
Identify why al-Tazi was special
Note the enumeration of his scholarly and spiritual attributes: imamate in Quranic sciences, linguistics, hadith, fiqh, sharp insight, and etiquette of saints.
This shows his comprehensive excellence.
3
Understand the proverbial sayings
Reflect on the saying 'he is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi' and the reaction of patience under harm. What does this reveal about his character?
Proverbs indicate he set the standard for intellect and forbearance.
4
Recognize Sanusi's connection
See how Sanusi's companionship with al-Tazi is described as a blessing, shared with other eminent figures like Ali al-Taluti and Ahmad Zarruq.
This emphasizes the value of association with such a saint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصوف وتربيته الأخلاقية هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي ظهر أنّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران. كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من هذا الجانب؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان ، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه . . كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في « نيل الابتهاج ) عن ابن صعد صاحب ( النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من جلالته وسعادته : أنَّ المثل ضرب بعقله وحلمه ، واشتهر في الآفاق ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن ؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال : كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي ، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال : لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا ؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق ، والصبر على المكاره ، واصطناع المعروف للناس ، والمداراة ، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه ، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته ، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة ، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة ؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة ، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار ((۱) وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي : صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل ، وانتسابه له ، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام ؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي ، والحافظ التنسي ، والإمام أحمد زروق قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في « البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » : ( أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح (1) انظر ( نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٦٠ ) ، وذكر أنه توفي سنة ( ٨٦٦هـ ) ، وإليه تنسب الطريقة التازية
His Sufism and moral upbringing: There are great spiritual figures who influenced Imam al-Sanūsī, but what appeared is that the shaykh, the saint, the gnostic, the righteous Ibrāhīm ibn Muḥammad ibn ʿAlī al-Tāzī, resident of Oran, was the one with the greatest impact on Imam al-Sanūsī from this aspect. For, in addition to his imamate in the sciences of the Qur'an, linguistics, memorization of ḥadīth, his wide knowledge of fiqh and its principles, and his sharpness of insight and understanding … he was endowed with the etiquette of the saints and the perfect ones. Al-ʿAllāmah al-Tinbuktī narrated in 'Nayl al-Ibtihāj' from Ibn Ṣaʿd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thāqib': "Sufficient for you regarding his majesty and felicity is that proverbs were made of his intellect and forbearance, and mention of his virtue and knowledge became famous in the horizons until now; when one exaggerates in describing a man, he says: 'He is like my master Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī', and when someone is filled with rage he says: 'If I were in the position of my master Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī, I would not have endured this'—because of what he used to bear of harm from people, patience upon hardships, doing good to people, and diplomacy. So he is one whom Allah manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller to spread his miracles, cloaked in the robe of love and awe, along with his acceptance in the hearts of the elite and the commoners. He called them to Allah with insight and guided them to His servitude through the doctrines of tawḥīd and the functions of dhikr." And it was among the blessings of Imam al-Sanūsī: his companionship with this noble gnostic and his affiliation to him. He was shared in this by eminent figures such as his maternal brother Shaykh ʿAlī al-Tālūtī, al-Ḥāfiẓ al-Tanasī, and Imam Aḥmad Zarrūq. The historian al-ʿAllāmah Ibn Maryam al-Malītī said in 'al-Bustān fī Dhikr al-Awliyāʾ wa al-ʿUlamāʾ bi-Tilimsān': "He took from the imam, the allamah, the saint, the ascetic, the sincere advisor…" (1) See 'Nayl al-Ibtihāj' p. 60, and it mentions that he died in the year 866 AH, and to him is attributed the Tāziyya order.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and spiritual description of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi and his influence on Imam Sanusi. It begins by stating that while many spiritual figures influenced Sanusi, it was Ibrahim al-Tazi who had the greatest impact on him in this regard. The passage then enumerates al-Tazi's qualifications: he was an imam in Quranic sciences, linguistics, hadith, fiqh and its principles, and had sharp insight. Moreover, he was endowed with the manners of saints. The author then quotes al-Tinbukti from Ibn Sa'd, who eulogizes al-Tazi's majesty, saying that his intellect and forbearance became proverbial—people compare others to him in virtue, and his patience in the face of harm is legendary. He was a guide for people, adorned with divine love and awe, and accepted by all. He called people to Allah with insight, teaching them tawhid and dhikr practices. The passage then notes that Sanusi was blessed to be his companion and affiliate. Others also shared this blessing, like Ali al-Taluti, al-Tanasi, and Ahmad Zarruq. Finally, it mentions Ibn Maryam's citation from al-Bustan, noting that al-Tazi died in 866 AH and the Taziyya order is named after him. This passage emphasizes the deep spiritual and scholarly debt Sanusi owed to al-Tazi.

Key Terms
إبراهيم التازي
نيل الابتهاج
البستان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Sanusi's education was only scholarly, with no spiritual dimension.
Correction: This passage highlights the equal importance of spiritual upbringing and sainthood, showing that al-Tazi's saintly character and moral example were central to Sanusi's formation.

Checkpoint
What was the character of Ibrahim al-Tazi that became proverbial, according to the passage?
A) His wealth and generosity
B) His intellect and forbearance
C) His knowledge of arithmetic
D) His lineage and ancestry

Key Takeaway
Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi's blend of scholarship and saintly patience made him the foremost spiritual guide for Imam Sanusi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are harmed by others, do your thoughts immediately turn to how you can endure like Ibrahim al-Tazi, or do you seek revenge? What one change can you make today to cultivate greater forbearance?
?
The passage says al-Tazi called people to Allah with insight and guided them by his character. Is your own life a silent call to Allah? What specific step will you take this week to make your character more inviting to truth?
?
You have learned that Sanusi's greatest spiritual influence was from a man known for patience and virtue, not just academic brilliance. If you were to consider the person who has shaped your faith the most, do they resemble al-Tazi more in their knowledge or their character? What does that reveal about your own priorities?

The Blessing of Spiritual Companionship
Biographical account of Sanusi's spiritual initiation and lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the khirqa initiation and the spiritual lineage connecting al-Sanusi to earlier saints.

Core Idea
Spiritual initiation through the khirqa connects teachers and students across generations.

This passage highlights the importance of spiritual lineage in Sufi tradition. Imam al-Sanusi's connection to the renowned saint Ibrahim al-Tazi is presented as a blessing, with a physical symbol—the khirqa—and a traditional blessing gesture. The text also traces al-Tazi's own spiritual chain back to the great saint Abu Madyan, underscoring the authenticity of the transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Let the biographical narrative come through.
Notice the use of terms like 'khirqa' and 'arif'.
2
Identify the key elements of initiation
The passage mentions two key actions: clothing with the khirqa and spitting in the mouth. Understand that these are symbolic acts of baraka transmission.
The spitting is a traditional blessing, not disrespect.
3
Trace the spiritual chain
Follow the chain: Ibrahim al-Tazi received khirqa from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, who received from al-Zawawi, who received from Abu Madyan. This chain establishes authority.
Chains like these are common in Sufi initiations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي : صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل ، وانتسابه له ، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام ؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي ، والحافظ التنسي ، والإمام أحمد زروق . قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في « البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » : ( أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران ؛ ألبسه الخرقة ، وحدثه بها عن شيوخه ، وبصق في فيه ، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة ) والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي ، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير
And it was among the blessings of Imam al-Sanusi: his companionship with this noble knower of God (ʿārif), and his affiliation to him; and notable figures shared with him in this, such as his maternal brother Shaykh ʿAlī al-Tālūtī, and al-Ḥāfiẓ al-Tanassī, and Imam Aḥmad Zarrūq. The historian scholar Ibn Maryam al-Malītī said in 'al-Bustān fī dhikr al-awliyāʾ wa al-ʿulamāʾ bi-Tilimsān': (He learned from the Imam, the scholar, the saint, the ascetic, the sincere advisor Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī, resident of Wahrān; he clothed him with the khirqa, and transmitted it to him from his shaykhs, and spat in his mouth, and related many things from him.) And the knower of God (ʿārif) al-Tāzī had worn the khirqa according to the way of the noble Sufis from Sharaf al-Dīn al-Dāʿī, and he wore it from Shaykh Ṣāliḥ ibn Muḥammad al-Zawāwī, by his chain to Abū Madyan, the famous knower of God and the great pole (quṭb).
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is biographical, describing Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual connection with the great saint Ibrahim al-Tazi. It begins by stating that among al-Sanusi's blessings was his companionship with this noble 'arif (gnostic), and that many other notable figures also shared that privilege. The passage then quotes the historian Ibn Maryam al-Maliti, who reports that al-Sanusi learned from al-Tazi, who clothed him with the khirqa (the Sufi cloak of initiation), transmitted it from his own shaykhs, and also performed the traditional act of blessing by spitting in his mouth (a practice associated with transmitting spiritual baraka). Finally, it traces al-Tazi's own spiritual lineage back through a chain of saints to the famous saint Abu Madyan, indicating the authenticity and prestige of the transmission.

Key Terms
خرقة (khirqa)
عارف (ʿārif)
قطب (quṭb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spitting in someone's mouth is a degrading act.
Correction: In Sufi tradition, spitting in the mouth is a symbolic act of transmitting spiritual blessing (baraka), not disrespect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Tazi do to al-Sanusi as a blessing gesture?
A) He gave him a book.
B) He spat in his mouth.
C) He appointed him as a teacher.
D) He wrote him a letter.

Key Takeaway
The khirqa and the blessing gesture symbolize the baraka transmitted from teacher to student in the Sufi tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you actively seek the companionship of those who are closer to Allah, or do you content yourself with knowledge alone? What steps will you take this week to connect with a spiritual guide?
?
The khirqa represents a chain of transmission going back centuries. Are you aware of your own spiritual lineage? If you died today, would you have passed on the blessings you received to others?
?
The passage mentions that al-Sanusi considered it a blessing to be in the company of the ʿārif. When was the last time you considered it a blessing to be in the company of a righteous person? How can you cultivate that appreciation starting today?

Al-Sanusi’s Esteemed Teacher: Al-Hasan Abrkan
Introduces al-Hasan Abrkan and relates al-Sanusi's praise and blessing anecdotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of al-Sanusi’s relationship with al-Hasan Abrkan and the blessing he received that confirmed his spiritual merit.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi found no saint like Abrkan, and a divine blessing marked him as pure.

This passage introduces one of al-Sanusi’s most cherished spiritual teachers: al-Hasan ibn Makhluf, known as Abrkan. It not only highlights al-Sanusi’s profound respect for him but also records a prophetic blessing and a childhood sign that foreshadowed al-Sanusi’s spiritual greatness. Let’s explore these anecdotes to appreciate the reverence accorded to al-Sanusi by his elders.

Guided Path
1
Meet al-Hasan Abrkan
Read the passage to learn who Abrkan was and how al-Sanusi described him.
Abrkan means 'the black' in Berber.
2
The blessing encounter
Notice the prayer Abrkan made for al-Sanusi and its fulfillment.
Ibn Maryam confirms that God verified the prayer.
3
The childhood sign
Understand the meaning of 'nuqra khāliṣa' and its significance.
It signifies innate spiritual purity.
4
Reflect on the pattern
Consider how these anecdotes establish al-Sanusi’s spiritual pedigree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها . الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي الراشدي ، شهر بأبركان ، ومعناه بلسان البربرية : الأسود ، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به ، وكان يقول : ( رأيت المشايخ والأولياء ، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان ) ، وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي تبسم له من الأئمة ، وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له : ( جعلك الله المتقين ) ، قال العلامة ابن مريم : ( فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته فيه ) وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد . . وضع يديه على رأسه وقال : نقرة خالصة !
And among the noble souls to whom the breaths of our Imam al-Sanusi were connected: the imam, the jurist, the great pole (quṭb) al-Ḥasan ibn Makhlūf ibn Masʿūd al-Mazīlī al-Rāshidī, known as Abrkan, and its meaning in the Berber language: the black; he accompanied him much and benefited from him, and he used to say: (I have seen the shaykhs and saints, but I have not seen anyone like my master al-Ḥasan Abrkan). And when Imam al-Sanusi entered upon him, he smiled at him from the imams, and initiated conversation with him, and said to him: (May God make you among the pious). The scholar Ibn Maryam said: (So God verified his perspicacity and supplication in him.) And in his childhood, when he would pass with the boys by Imam Ibn Marzuq al-Ḥafīd... he would place his hands on his head and say: A pure piece! (nuqra khāliṣa).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage introduces another spiritual influence on al-Sanusi: al-Hasan ibn Makhluf, known as Abrkan (meaning 'the black' in Berber). It states that al-Sanusi accompanied him extensively and benefited, and that al-Sanusi himself declared he had never seen anyone like him among the shaykhs and saints. The passage then relates a specific interaction: whenever al-Sanusi would enter upon Abrkan, Abrkan would smile, initiate conversation, and pray for him to be among the pious (al-muttaqīn). Ibn Maryam confirms that this prayer was fulfilled. Finally, a childhood incident is recounted: when the young al-Sanusi passed by Imam Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid among other boys, Ibn Marzuq would place his hands on his head and call him 'a pure piece' (nuqra khāliṣa), indicating his innate spiritual purity and future distinction.

Key Terms
أبركان (Abrkan)
نقرة خالصة (nuqra khāliṣa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The gesture of placing hands on the head is a form of test or examination.
Correction: It is a blessing and recognition of spiritual purity, not a test.

Checkpoint
What did Ibn Marzuq say about the young al-Sanusi when he passed by?
A) He is a scholar.
B) He is a pure piece.
C) He is a saint.
D) He is a teacher.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi's spiritual station was recognized early by his teachers, as shown by Abrkan's prayer and Ibn Marzuq's blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone sees spiritual potential in you, do you take it as a burden or a gift? Al-Sanusi's teachers recognized his purity and blessed him. Have you ever received a sincere blessing from someone who saw goodness in you? What did you do with it, and what will you do today to honor that trust?
?
Al-Sanusi was called 'a pure piece' as a child. If a scholar looked at your heart right now, would they still see that same purity? What has dulled your spiritual luster, and what concrete step will you take this week to polish it again?
?
Al-Sanusi said he never saw a saint like Abrkan. Is there anyone in your life who inspires that kind of awe in faith? If not, are you surrounding yourself with people who draw you closer to God? Will you seek out such a person this month, even if it means stepping out of your comfort zone?

Ibrahim al-Tazi: The Transmission of the Sufi Cloak
Transmission of the khirqa from Ibrahim al-Tazi to Sanusi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Ibrahim al-Tazi in transmitting the Sufi cloak (khirqa) to Imam al-Sanusi and the significance of this spiritual lineage.

Core Idea
The khirqa connects Sanusi to a chain of spiritual masters reaching back to Abu Madyan.

In traditional Islamic learning, spiritual transmission is as important as textual knowledge. Imam al-Sanusi received the Sufi cloak from Ibrahim al-Tazi, who himself inherited it through a chain of saints. This lesson introduces the concept of the khirqa and the masters who transmitted it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Ibrahim al-Tazi
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the key actions: bestowing the khirqa, narrating, and spitting.
Spitting is a blessing practice.
2
Understand the chain of transmission
Trace the chain: Ibrahim al-Tazi received from Sharf al-Din al-Da'i, who received from Salih al-Zawawi, who received from Abu Madyan.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this lineage matters for Sanusi's authority as a scholar and spiritual guide.
It connects him to the great poles of Sufism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران ؛ ألبسه الخرقة ، وحدثه بها عن شيوخه ، وبصق في فيه ، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة . والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي ، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير . ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها . الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي الراشدي ، شهر بأبركان ، ومعناه بلسان البربرية : الأسود ، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به ، وكان يقول : ( رأيت المشايخ والأولياء ، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان ) ، وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي تبسم له من الأئمة، وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له : ( جعلك الله المتقين ) ، قال العلامة ابن مريم : ( فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته فيه ) . وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد . . وضع يديه على رأسه وقال : نقرة خالصة !
Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Wahran; he clothed him with the cloak (khirqa), and narrated to him from his shaykhs, and spat in his mouth, and narrated many things from him. And the knower (al-ʿārif) al-Tazi had worn the cloak according to the method of the noble Sufis from Sharf al-Dīn al-Dāʿī, and he wore it from al-Shaykh Ṣāliḥ ibn Muḥammad al-Zawāwī through his chain to Abū Madyan, the famous knower and the great pole (al-quṭb al-kabīr). And among the noble souls to which the breaths of our Imām al-Sanūsī were connected: the imām, the jurist, and the great pole al-Ḥasan ibn Makhlūf ibn Masʿūd al-Mazīlī al-Rāshidī, known as Abarkan, meaning in the Berber language: the black; he accompanied him much and benefited from him, and he used to say: 'I have seen the shaykhs and the saints, but I have not seen anyone like my master al-Ḥasan Abarkan.' And when Imām al-Sanūsī entered upon him, he smiled at him from the imāms, and opened speech with him, and said to him: 'May God make you among the righteous.' Al-ʿAllāma Ibn Maryam said: 'So God verified his insight and his supplication in him.' And in his childhood, when he passed with the boys by Imām Ibn Marzūq the grandson, he placed his hands on his head and said: 'A pure piece!'
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides biographical information about two shaykhs who were spiritual influences on Imam al-Sanusi: Ibrahim al-Tazi and al-Hasan Abarkan. It begins with Ibrahim al-Tazi, who bestowed the Sufi cloak (khirqa) upon him through a chain tracing back to Abu Madyan. The mention of spitting in the mouth is a traditional practice of blessing. Then it describes al-Hasan Abarkan, a jurist and great spiritual pole, whose name means 'black' in Berber. Sanusi benefited greatly from him, and Abarkan recognized Sanusi's special status through his smile and prayer. The passage also records an incident from Sanusi's childhood when Imam Ibn Marzuq the grandson called him 'a pure piece', indicating early recognition of his potential. The commentary explains the significance of the khirqa transmission and the spiritual relationship between Sanusi and these masters.

Key Terms
الخرقة (khirqa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The act of spitting in Sanusi's mouth was a form of disrespect or a literal test.
Correction: In the Sufi tradition, spitting in the mouth (blessing by saliva) is a practice of transmitting spiritual blessing (baraka) from master to disciple.

Checkpoint
What did Ibrahim al-Tazi do when he met Imam al-Sanusi?
A) Gave him a book
B) Bestowed the khirqa and spat in his mouth
C) Sent him to another shaykh
D) Taught him jurisprudence

Key Takeaway
Ibrahim al-Tazi transmitted the Sufi cloak to Sanusi through a blessed lineage reaching back to Abu Madyan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about a spiritual chain that transmitted the khirqa from Abu Madyan to al-Sanusi. This chain implies that al-Sanusi did not seek knowledge or spiritual blessing in isolation. How does your own search for truth connect you to the scholars and saints of the past? Are you actively seeking living teachers who can transmit this blessing, or are you relying solely on books and your own intellect? Commit to one concrete step to attach yourself to a living chain of guidance.
?
The act of spitting in the mouth, though strange to modern sensibilities, was a profound transmission of barakah. It required humility and trust from the recipient. When was the last time you submitted to a spiritual practice that felt uncomfortable or humbling? Are there practices of the righteous predecessors that you avoid because they seem outdated or odd? Choose one such practice and commit to doing it with sincere intention, seeking the barakah behind the form.
?
The chain ends with al-Sanusi, who became a great scholar himself. The blessing he received was not for personal prestige but to enable him to serve and guide others. How are you using the knowledge and spiritual gifts you have received—from your teachers, your family, or your community—to serve others? Write down one specific way you will pass on a blessing you have received before this week ends.

Al-Hasan Abarkan: The Great Pole Who Saw Sanusi's Destiny
Biographical account of al-Hasan Abarkan and his recognition of Sanusi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the special relationship between Imam al-Sanusi and al-Hasan Abarkan, and how Abarkan's recognition and prayer shaped Sanusi's spiritual path.

Core Idea
Al-Hasan Abarkan recognized Sanusi's potential and prayed for him, fulfilling his destiny as a righteous scholar.

Beyond formal chains of transmission, spiritual masters often saw the potential in great scholars from childhood. This lesson explores the role of al-Hasan Abarkan, a great pole (quṭb), who blessed and recognized Sanusi's future greatness, as well as an earlier incident with Ibn Marzuq.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about al-Hasan Abarkan
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note Abarkan's name meaning and his status as a great pole.
2
Understand Sanusi's admiration
Sanusi said he never saw anyone like Abarkan among the saints. Reflect on what that means.
Abarkan was a great jurist and spiritual pole.
3
Recognize Abarkan's prayer
Abarkan smiled, opened speech, and prayed for Sanusi to be among the righteous. Notice the fulfillment noted by Ibn Maryam.
4
Consider the childhood incident
Ibn Marzuq the grandson called young Sanusi 'a pure piece'. This shows early recognition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران ؛ ألبسه الخرقة ، وحدثه بها عن شيوخه ، وبصق في فيه ، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة . والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي ، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير . ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها . الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي الراشدي ، شهر بأبركان ، ومعناه بلسان البربرية : الأسود ، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به ، وكان يقول : ( رأيت المشايخ والأولياء ، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان ) ، وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي تبسم له من الأئمة، وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له : ( جعلك الله المتقين ) ، قال العلامة ابن مريم : ( فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته فيه ) . وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد . . وضع يديه على رأسه وقال : نقرة خالصة !
Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Wahran; he clothed him with the cloak (khirqa), and narrated to him from his shaykhs, and spat in his mouth, and narrated many things from him. And the knower (al-ʿārif) al-Tazi had worn the cloak according to the method of the noble Sufis from Sharf al-Dīn al-Dāʿī, and he wore it from al-Shaykh Ṣāliḥ ibn Muḥammad al-Zawāwī through his chain to Abū Madyan, the famous knower and the great pole (al-quṭb al-kabīr). And among the noble souls to which the breaths of our Imām al-Sanūsī were connected: the imām, the jurist, and the great pole al-Ḥasan ibn Makhlūf ibn Masʿūd al-Mazīlī al-Rāshidī, known as Abarkan, meaning in the Berber language: the black; he accompanied him much and benefited from him, and he used to say: 'I have seen the shaykhs and the saints, but I have not seen anyone like my master al-Ḥasan Abarkan.' And when Imām al-Sanūsī entered upon him, he smiled at him from the imāms, and opened speech with him, and said to him: 'May God make you among the righteous.' Al-ʿAllāma Ibn Maryam said: 'So God verified his insight and his supplication in him.' And in his childhood, when he passed with the boys by Imām Ibn Marzūq the grandson, he placed his hands on his head and said: 'A pure piece!'
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides biographical information about two shaykhs who were spiritual influences on Imam al-Sanusi: Ibrahim al-Tazi and al-Hasan Abarkan. It begins with Ibrahim al-Tazi, who bestowed the Sufi cloak (khirqa) upon him through a chain tracing back to Abu Madyan. The mention of spitting in the mouth is a traditional practice of blessing. Then it describes al-Hasan Abarkan, a jurist and great spiritual pole, whose name means 'black' in Berber. Sanusi benefited greatly from him, and Abarkan recognized Sanusi's special status through his smile and prayer. The passage also records an incident from Sanusi's childhood when Imam Ibn Marzuq the grandson called him 'a pure piece', indicating early recognition of his potential. The commentary explains the significance of the khirqa transmission and the spiritual relationship between Sanusi and these masters.

Key Terms
القطب الكبير (al-quṭb al-kabīr)
أبركان (Abarkan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Hasan Abarkan say to Imam al-Sanusi when he entered upon him?
A) 'You are a great scholar'
B) 'May God make you among the righteous'
C) 'Sit down'
D) 'I have seen many saints but not like you'

Key Takeaway
Al-Hasan Abarkan and Ibn Marzuq both recognized Sanusi's spiritual potential through prayer and blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever encountered someone whose spiritual potential was clear to you, but you failed to pray for them as Al-Hasan Abarkan did for Sanusi? What stops you from being a source of blessing for others today?
?
Ibn Marzuq recognized Sanusi's purity even in childhood. Do you look for the 'pure pieces' in the people you meet, or do you judge by outward appearances? How can you train your heart to see the hidden goodness in others?
?
Sanusi said he had not seen anyone like Abarkan among the saints. Who has been a spiritual mentor or role model in your life, and have you expressed gratitude to them? If not, what specific step will you take this week to honor that person?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

Sanusi's Sufism and Self-Reflection
Sanusi's love for Sufism and a self-referential quote.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's deep commitment to Sufism as a path of action and his recognition of the rarity of a scholar who masters both outward and inward knowledge.

Core Idea
Sufism is a path of action, not just words.

Before we examine Sanusi's scholarly lineage, we must first understand his spiritual orientation. This passage reveals his love for Sufism and his own awareness of his unique position as a scholar who combined exoteric and esoteric knowledge. His student's commentary suggests he was speaking of himself, hinting at his exceptional status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Sufism
Read the first part of the source text, from 'ويظهر أن محبة الصوفية' to 'فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك'. Notice the emphasis on action over speech.
The phrase 'ليست بطريق قال بل جد ومثابرة وفعال' is key.
2
Analyze Sanusi's quote
Consider why Sanusi describes a scholar combining outward and inward knowledge as extremely rare. What does he advise those who find such a person?
3
Reflect on al-Mallālī's comment
Al-Mallālī interprets the quote as self-reference. Consider the humility or self-awareness this might imply.
This is a common point of reflection in biographical works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويظهر أن محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم ، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال ، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال ، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها ، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه : ( من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن على أكمل وجه ؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين ، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور ، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى ، فليشدَّ عليه يده ؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً ) . عقب على هذه الكلمة الشيخ الملالي تلميذ الإمام : ( وكأنه أشار به لنفسه ، فلم يلبث بعده حتى خطف ، ولا شك أنه لا يوجد مثله أبداً ) . فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك . وقال العلامة الشفشاوني : ( وأشياخه وأشياخ ابن زكري واحد ومن أشياخهما العالم الرحال الأَيْلَّيُّ ، بسكون اللام وفتح الهمزة وضم الياء وكسر اللام ، وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة ، والشيخ ابن مرزوق شارح « البردة » ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن العباس شارح « لامية ابن مالك » ، والشيخ أبو العباس أحمد بن زاغ ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله أقرقار ، والشيخ أبو عثمان قاسم العقباني ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن الجلاب ، أفادني بذلك شيخنا أبو عبد الله محمد شقرون بن هبة الله )
And it appears that love of Sufism had permeated his heart, so he strove earnestly for leadership in their path—and it is not a path of saying, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action—and therefore you find complaint about its carpet being folded up, until Imām al-Sanūsī himself said: 'Among the strange things in our time is that there exists a scholar who has been given the knowledge of the outward and the inward in the most complete manner, such that benefit is derived from him in both fields. His existence is extremely rare. Whoever finds him has found a great treasure, worldly and otherworldly. So let him hold fast to him, lest he be lost soon and he never finds his like east or west forever.' Al-Shaykh al-Mallālī, the student of the Imam, commented on this statement: 'As if he was pointing to himself. He did not remain long after that until he was taken, and there is no doubt that his like will never exist.' So it is as if he revealed to us by that. And al-ʿAllāma al-Shafshāwnī said: 'His shaykhs and the shaykhs of Ibn Zakrī are one. Among their shaykhs is the traveler scholar al-Ayllī (with sukun of lām, fatḥa of hamza, ḍamma of yā, kasra of lām), and he is the first to introduce the science of kalām (ʿilm al-kalām) to the Maghreb in later times; and al-Shaykh Ibn Marzūq, commentator on al-Burda; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh ibn al-ʿAbbās, commentator on Lāmiyyat Ibn Mālik; and al-Shaykh Abū al-ʿAbbās Aḥmad ibn Zāgh; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh Aqrqār; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿUthmān Qāsim al-ʿUqbānī; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh ibn al-Jallāb. My shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh Muḥammad Shaqrūn ibn Hibat Allāh informed me of that.'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological account. It first comments on Imam al-Sanusi's deep love for Sufism, emphasizing that it is a path of action, not mere talk. It then quotes Sanusi himself, who remarks on the extreme rarity of a scholar combining both exoteric and esoteric knowledge, urging one who finds such a person to hold onto him. The author notes that Sanusi's student al-Mallālī interpreted this as Sanusi referring to himself, and indeed he died soon after. This suggests Sanusi's own self-awareness of his unique status. Finally, al-Shafshāwnī lists Sanusi's teachers, noting that one of them, al-Ayllī, was the first to introduce the science of kalām to the Maghreb in later times. The list includes well-known figures such as Ibn Marzūq (commentator on al-Burda) and others. This establishes Sanusi's scholarly lineage in both Sufism and kalām.

Key Terms
محبة الصوفية
علم الظاهر والباطن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi's statement about a rare scholar is a boastful claim of his own superiority.
Correction: The statement is presented as a general observation about the rarity of such scholars. Al-Mallālī's interpretation may be speculative, and the tone suggests humility rather than boasting. Sanusi is describing an ideal, not necessarily claiming it for himself outright.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the path of Sufism?
A) It is a path of saying (qaal).
B) It is a path of action (jidd, muthabara, fi'āl).
C) It is a path of solitude.
D) It is a path of scholarship only.

Key Takeaway
Sufism is a path of action, and Sanusi saw the combination of outward and inward knowledge as extremely rare.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Sufism is 'not a path of saying, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action.' In which area of your life—your worship, your character, your learning—have you been content with mere words (saying) rather than actual effort? What one concrete action will you take today to move from 'saying' to 'doing'?
?
Sanusi marveled at the extreme rarity of a scholar who masters both outward and inward knowledge. If you were to be such a person, how would your priorities have to change? What would you need to sacrifice or pursue? Be honest: are you even aiming for that combination, or do you settle for only one side?
?
Al-Mallālī interpreted Sanusi's words as a self-reference, as if he was revealing his own status. Have you ever recognized a truth about yourself that you wished others would see? Do you fear being seen as you truly are? What holds you back from authentic self-disclosure?

Sanusi's Teachers and the Spread of Kalam
Listing of Sanusi's teachers and al-Ayllī's role in kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will identify key teachers of Imam al-Sanusi and understand the role of al-Ayllī in introducing the science of kalam to the Maghreb.

Core Idea
Al-Ayllī was the first to bring kalam to the Maghreb in later times.

After exploring Sanusi's inner spiritual drive, we now turn to his scholarly lineage. This passage lists his teachers, highlighting that many were shared with another scholar, Ibn Zakrī. Notably, al-Ayllī is credited with pioneering the introduction of ʿilm al-kalām to the Maghreb in the later period, a key detail for understanding the transmission of theological discourse.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of teachers
Read the second part of the source text starting from 'وقال العلامة الشفشاوني'. Note the names and any descriptors.
Pay attention to the description of al-Ayllī: 'وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة'.
2
Identify al-Ayllī's significance
Al-Ayllī is described as the first to introduce kalam to the Maghreb in later times. Consider why this is important for the history of Islamic theology.
This connects Sanusi's training to the broader tradition of kalam.
3
Connect to the course theme
Reflect on how Sanusi's teachers, especially al-Ayllī, influenced his own kalam works. This passage establishes his scholarly credentials.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it appears that love of Sufism had permeated his heart, so he strove earnestly for leadership in their path—and it is not a path of saying, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action—and therefore you find complaint about its carpet being folded up, until Imām al-Sanūsī himself said: 'Among the strange things in our time is that there exists a scholar who has been given the knowledge of the outward and the inward in the most complete manner, such that benefit is derived from him in both fields. His existence is extremely rare. Whoever finds him has found a great treasure, worldly and otherworldly. So let him hold fast to him, lest he be lost soon and he never finds his like east or west forever.' Among their shaykhs is the traveler scholar al-Ayllī (with sukun of lām, fatḥa of hamza, ḍamma of yā, kasra of lām), and he is the first to introduce the science of kalām (ʿilm al-kalām) to the Maghreb in later times; and al-Shaykh Ibn Marzūq, commentator on al-Burda; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh ibn al-ʿAbbās, commentator on Lāmiyyat Ibn Mālik; and al-Shaykh Abū al-ʿAbbās Aḥmad ibn Zāgh; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh Aqrqār; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿUthmān Qāsim al-ʿUqbānī; and al-Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh ibn al-Jallāb. ?

?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

Sanusi's Self-Referential Rarity Statement
Biographer describes Sanusi's Sufi devotion, quotes his marvel statement, and al-Mallali's interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi's student interpreted his statement about a rare scholar as referring to Sanusi himself, highlighting his exceptional status.

Core Idea
Sanusi's description of a rare scholar was actually about himself.

This lesson presents a biographical anecdote from Sanusi's life. It shows not only his dedication to Sufism but also a remarkable statement he made about a rare scholar, which his student later interpreted as a self-reference. The passage gives us a glimpse into Sanusi's own self-perception and the esteem in which he was held.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then read the English translation. Notice the flow from biographical context to Sanusi's statement to the student's commentary.
This is a short passage, so take time to absorb each part.
2
Understand the context: Sanusi's love for Sufism
The opening lines describe how Sanusi's heart was captivated by Sufism, leading him to strive earnestly in the Sufi path. Understand that this sets the stage for his later statement.
Sufism here refers to Islamic mysticism, emphasizing spiritual purification.
3
Focus on Sanusi's statement about the rare scholar
Read Sanusi's words carefully. He describes a scholar who masters both outward and inward sciences, extremely rare, a great treasure. Notice the urgency: 'hold fast to him lest he be lost.'
Consider: why would Sanusi emphasize rarity and loss?
4
Examine al-Mallali's commentary
Al-Mallali, Sanusi's student, interprets the statement as self-referential: 'It is as if he referred to himself.' He says Sanusi died shortly after, and no one like him ever existed. Reflect on the boldness of this interpretation.
Al-Mallali's comment reveals his conviction about Sanusi's uniqueness.
5
Reflect on the biographical significance
Consider how this anecdote shapes our understanding of Sanusi's character and his students' perception. What does it say about his humility or his awareness of his own status?
This is a rare glimpse into self-perception within Islamic scholarly tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويظهر أن محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه: (من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن على أكمل وجه؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى، فليشدَّ عليه يده؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً). عقب على هذه الكلمة الشيخ الملالي تلميذ الإمام: (وكأنه أشار به لنفسه، فلم يلبث بعده حتى خطف، ولا شك أنه لا يوجد مثله أبداً). فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك
It appears that the love of Sufism had captivated his heart, so he strove diligently to take the lead in their path, and it is not a path of mere speech but of seriousness, perseverance, and action. Therefore you find the complaint is folded up, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the marvels of our time is that there exists a scholar who has been granted knowledge of the outward and inward in the most complete manner, such that benefit is derived from him in both sciences. The existence of his like is extremely rare, so whoever finds him has found a great treasure in this world and the next. Let him hold fast to him, lest he be lost soon and never find his like in East or West ever again.' Sheikh al-Mallali, a student of the Imam, commented on this statement: 'It is as if he referred to himself; he did not remain after that for long before he was taken, and there is no doubt that there is no one like him ever.' It is as if he informed us of that.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote about Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by noting that his love for Sufism had captivated his heart, leading him to strive earnestly to excel in the Sufi path—a path characterized not by mere speech but by serious effort, perseverance, and action. The biographer then remarks that complaints are folded up (i.e., there is no room for complaint), setting the stage for Sanusi's own statement. Sanusi then says: 'Among the marvels of our time is that there exists a scholar who has been granted knowledge of the outward and inward in the most complete manner, such that benefit is derived from him in both sciences. The existence of his like is extremely rare. Whoever finds him has found a great treasure in this world and the next. He should hold fast to him, lest he be lost soon and never find his like ever again.' The student of Sanusi, Shaykh al-Mallali, commented on this statement, saying that it seemed Sanusi was referring to himself, for he did not remain long after that before he died, and there is no doubt that there will never be anyone like him. The biographer concludes that it is as if Sanusi was informing us of this through his words. Thus, the passage highlights Sanusi's exceptional status and the recognition of his own rarity by his student.

Key Terms
محبة الصوفية
طريق الصوفية
علم الظاهر
علم الباطن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi was describing another scholar.
Correction: Al-Mallali interpreted that Sanusi was referring to himself.

Checkpoint
What did al-Mallali interpret Sanusi's statement about the rare scholar to mean?
A) He was referring to a contemporary scholar
B) He was referring to himself
C) He was referring to a future scholar
D) He was referring to the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's student revealed that his teacher's description of a rare scholar was actually a self-portrait, emphasizing his unique stature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were the most knowledgeable scholar in your community, would you be able to humbly acknowledge your own rarity like Sanusi did? What stops you from honestly assessing your own gifts without falling into arrogance or false modesty?
?
Al-Mallali realized that Sanusi's description of a rare scholar was actually about himself. Think of something you have said about others—does it actually reveal something about yourself? What would your closest friend say about how you see yourself?
?
Sanusi urged holding fast to a rare scholar before he is lost. Who in your life is a 'treasure' you have taken for granted? Write down one specific step you will take this week to appreciate and learn from them before it is too late.

Sanusi's Teachers and the Introduction of Kalam to the Maghrib
Al-Shafshawni enumerates Sanusi's teachers and notes the first introducer of kalam to the Maghrib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage of Imam al-Sanusi and the role of al-Aylī in bringing the science of kalam to the Maghrib.

Core Idea
Sanusi's teachers connect him to the first introducer of kalam in the Maghrib.

Al-Shafshawni, a later scholar, provides a valuable list of Sanusi's teachers, highlighting their scholarly achievements and connections. This passage not only names key figures but also notes that one of them, al-Aylī, was the first to introduce the science of kalam (theology) to the Maghrib in later times. Understanding this lineage helps us appreciate the transmission of knowledge in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the teachers mentioned and note any additional information given about them.
Pay attention to the pronunciation guide for al-Aylī.
2
Identify the key figure al-Aylī
Al-Aylī is highlighted as the first to bring kalam to the Maghrib. Reflect on why this might be significant for Sanusi's education.
3
Reflect on scholarly chains
Consider how this list of teachers shows the interconnectedness of scholars and the importance of learning from multiple masters.
Sanusi and Ibn Zakari share teachers, indicating a common scholarly network.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال العلامة الشفشاوني: (وأشياخه وأشياخ ابن زكري واحد ومن أشياخهما العالم الرحال الأَيْلَّيُّ، بسكون اللام وفتح الهمزة وضم الياء وكسر اللام، وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة، والشيخ ابن مرزوق شارح «البردة»، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن العباس شارح «لامية ابن مالك»، والشيخ أبو العباس أحمد بن زاغ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله أقرقار، والشيخ أبو عثمان قاسم العقباني، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن الجلاب، أفادني بذلك شيخنا أبو عبد الله محمد شقرون بن هبة الله)
And the scholar al-Shafshawni said: 'His teachers and the teachers of Ibn Zakari are one, and among their teachers is the traveling scholar al-Aylī (with a sukun on the lam, fath on the hamza, damm on the ya, and kasr on the lam), and he is the first to introduce the science of kalam into the Maghrib in later times, and Sheikh Ibn Marzuq the commentator of al-Burda, and Sheikh Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas the commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik, and Sheikh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zag, and Sheikh Abu Abdullah Aqraqar, and Sheikh Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani, and Sheikh Abu Abdullah ibn al-Jallab. This was conveyed to me by our teacher Abu Abdullah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah.'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from the scholar al-Shafshawni listing the teachers of Imam al-Sanusi. He begins by stating that Sanusi and Ibn Zakari share the same teachers. He then mentions the traveling scholar al-Aylī, providing a detailed pronunciation guide for his name, and notes that al-Aylī was the first to introduce the science of kalam into the Maghrib in later times. After this, he lists other teachers: Ibn Marzuq, the commentator of the Burda; Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, the commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik; Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zag; Abu Abdullah Aqraqar; Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani; and Abu Abdullah ibn al-Jallab. Finally, al-Shafshawni attributes this information to his own teacher, Abu Abdullah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah. This passage demonstrates the scholarly lineage and connections of Sanusi.

Correction: The passage explicitly gives the pronunciation: sukun on lam, fath on hamza, damm on ya, kasr on lam, yielding 'al-Aylī'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Al-Zarruq: A Distinguished Student of Imam al-Sanusi
Al-Zarruq identified as a student of al-Sanusi despite being a contemporary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that even though Al-Zarruq was a contemporary and shared teachers with al-Sanusi, he still formally studied under him, as he himself affirmed.

Core Idea
Al-Zarruq was both a peer and a student of Imam al-Sanusi.

This brief biographical note introduces us to a remarkable figure: Ahmad al-Zarruq, a scholar of high rank who was among the contemporaries of Imam al-Sanusi. Yet, despite his stature and shared teachers, he placed himself as a student under al-Sanusi. Let us examine what this tells us about the transmission of knowledge and the humility of scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then its English translation. Notice the key descriptors of al-Zarruq.
2
Identify the central claim
The passage explicitly states that al-Zarruq studied under al-Sanusi. Find the phrase that indicates this.
The verb 'تلمذ' means he became a student.
3
Notice the surprising context
Al-Zarruq was a contemporary and even shared teachers with al-Sanusi. Why is it remarkable that he studied under him?
It shows that learning is not limited to rank or age.
4
Confirm the evidence
The passage says al-Zarruq himself affirmed his studentship, and this is recorded by historian al-Tanbakti. This solidifies the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان ممن تتلمذ للإمام السنوسي وهو من جملة أقرانه ، وأعيان أهل زمانه .. الإمام الشيخ العارف بالله تعالى أحمد بن أحمد البرنسي الفاسي المعروف بـ ( زروق ) ، والمتوفى سنة ( ٨٩٩هـ ) على جلالة شأنه وعلو قدره ، وقد شاركه في كثير من شيوخه ، وقد نص على التلمذة للإمام السنوسي بنفسه كما نقل ذلك المؤرخ العلامة التنبكتي (۲)

And he shared many of his teachers, and he himself affirmed studying under Imam al-Sanusi, as transmitted by the historian al-Tanbakti (2).

Commentary
This passage identifies Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Barnusi al-Fasi, famously known as Zarruq, as a student of Imam al-Sanusi. The passage emphasizes that al-Zarruq himself explicitly stated that he studied under al-Sanusi, and this statement is recorded by the historian al-Tanbakti. The footnote marker (2) likely refers to the source of this information. The inclusion of al-Zarruq's death year (899 AH) and his epithets ('the knower of Allah') underscores his scholarly stature.

Al-Balawi Witnesses al-Sanusi's Teaching Circle
Al-Balawi describes attending al-Sanusi's gatherings and the recitation of the Small Creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique teaching environment of Imam al-Sanusi as witnessed by al-Balawi, including the communal recitation of his Small Creed and the intense demand for his knowledge.

Core Idea
Al-Balawi's account shows al-Sanusi's teaching overwhelmed with seekers, yet still fostering deep devotion.

This lesson presents a rare eyewitness description of Imam al-Sanusi's teaching circle. Al-Balawi, a scholar who attended but never studied directly under him, provides vivid details of how al-Sanusi taught the Quran and hadith, and how his 'Small Creed' was recited by heart by students and commoners after Friday Asr prayer. This account highlights the widespread reverence and the intense demand for al-Sanusi's knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Balawi's Account
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the setting: the mosque near al-Sanusi's house, the packed gathering, and the recitation of Quran in seven modes and Sahih al-Bukhari.
Al-Balawi was not a direct student but an attendee.
2
Focus on the Small Creed Recitation
Observe how al-Sanusi's 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' was recited: students and common people recited it by heart in unison after Friday Asr prayer, a weekly habit. Reflect on what this tells about the creed's importance and accessibility.
This practice shows the creed was memorized and recited communally.
3
Reflect on al-Balawi's Regret
Al-Balawi laments not being able to read directly to al-Sanusi because students occupied all his time, using a sand clock to manage sessions. Why did al-Balawi fail to secure a slot? What does this say about the scholarly atmosphere?
Al-Sanusi's death prevented al-Balawi from fulfilling his wish.

ومن جملة الأعلام الذين اجتمعوا به ، وحضروا عموم مجالسه دون القراءة عليه مباشرةً : أبو جعفر أحمد بن علي البلوي الوادي آشي . المتوفى سنة ( ٩٣٨هـ ) ، وقد أرَّخَ له ولسيرته العطرة في « ثبته » المشهور ، ومن جملة ما قاله : ( لقيته رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وحضرت مجلسه الغاص بالمستفيدين من طلبة العلم والعامة بمسجده قرب داره بدرب مسوفة من داخل تلمسان أمَّنَها الله تعالى ، وحضرت الفاتحة » وأوائل سورة ( البقرة » تقرأ عليه بالسبع ، وكتباً غير ذلك ؛ منها « البخاري » ، كان يُقرأ عليه في بعض مجالس حضرتها ، ويتكلَّم على أحاديثه بالكلام الذي يدلُّ على مقامه في العلم والعبادة وغيره من كُتب المجلس 6 وحضرنا - يومَ سلمنا عليه إثرَ ما صلينا العصر خلفه ـ « عقيدته الصغرى » تقرأ بين يديه ، يقرؤها طلبته وجمع من العوام الملازمين لمجلسه عن ظهر قلب سرداً على صوتٍ واحد إثر سلامِهِ من صلاة عصر الجمعة عادة مستمرة ، وهو قاعد بمحرابه ، مقبل على الذكر ) (1) . يوم وقال : ( ولم تقدَّر لي القراءة عليه مع رغبتي في ذلك عليه ؛ لاستغراق طلبته أوقات قعوده ، حتى إنهم كانوا يقرؤون عليه والرملية في يد أحدهم إذا فرغت قطع ، وكنت أؤمل القراءة وأترصد لها وقتاً ، فعاجلته - قدَّسَهُ الله تعالى - المَنِيَّةُ ، ولم أنل من ذلك الأُمْنِيَّة ) (۲) وحرصي
And among the eminent people who met with him and attended his general gatherings without reading directly to him was Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Ali al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashi, who died in the year (938 AH). He recorded his (al-Sanusi's) biography and his fragrant life in his famous 'Thabt'. Among what he said: 'I met him, may Allah be pleased with him, and attended his gathering packed with beneficiaries from students of knowledge and the common people in his mosque near his house in Darb Masufa inside Tlemcen, may Allah protect it. And I attended the recitation of al-Fatiha and the beginnings of Surat al-Baqarah recited to him in the seven modes, and other books, including al-Bukhari, which was recited to him in some gatherings I attended, and he would comment on its hadiths with speech that indicated his station in knowledge and worship, and other books of the gathering. And we attended — on the day we greeted him after praying Asr behind him — his 'Small Creed' being read in his presence; his students and a group of common people who adhered to his gathering recited it by heart, as one voice, after his greeting from the Friday Asr prayer, a continuous habit, while he sat in his prayer niche, turning to remembrance.' (1) He also said: 'I was not able to read to him despite my desire for that, because his students occupied all his sitting times, such that they would read to him while the sand clock was in the hand of one of them; when it ran out, he would stop. I hoped to read and watched for a time, but death hastened to him — may Allah sanctify him — and I did not obtain that wish.' (2) And my eagerness...
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed eyewitness account from Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, who attended al-Sanusi's gatherings but did not directly read to him. Al-Balawi recorded this in his well-known work 'Thabt'. The account describes the packed nature of al-Sanusi's mosque in Tlemcen, where students and common people gathered. Al-Balawi observed recitations of Quran in the seven modes and books like Sahih al-Bukhari, with al-Sanusi commenting on hadiths in a way that displayed his exceptional knowledge and devotion. A particularly striking scene is the recitation of al-Sanusi's own work, 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' (the Small Creed), by students and laypeople in unison after the Friday Asr prayer, a regular practice with al-Sanusi seated in his prayer niche. However, al-Balawi regrets never having had the opportunity to study directly under him because the students monopolized all his time, using a sand clock to manage sessions. Before al-Balawi could find an opening, al-Sanusi passed away. The passage ends with al-Balawi's expression of eagerness.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that al-Balawi was a direct student who read to al-Sanusi.
Correction: Al-Balawi attended gatherings but did not read directly to him; he laments this missed opportunity.

Checkpoint

C) It was recited only by advanced students
D) It was read from books

Key Takeaway
Al-Balawi's account offers a lived portrait of al-Sanusi's teaching, where students and laypeople recited his creed by heart, showing the deep integration of theology into daily worship and the intense demand for his guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Balawi deeply regretted missing the chance to read directly to al-Sanusi because he waited for a convenient time. Are you postponing seeking beneficial knowledge, assuming you have more time? What specific step will you take this week to learn from a qualified teacher before your opportunity passes?
?
The common people in al-Sanusi's circle recited the Small Creed by heart. Do you have a core text of 'aqida memorized and ready to recite? If not, which creed will you commit to memory starting today, and when will you recite it?
?
When you attend a gathering of remembrance or study, do you participate actively like the students who recited in unison, or do you remain a spectator? How can you change that in your next opportunity?

Al-Sanusi's Major Theological Works
Al-Mallali enumerates the major theological works of Imam al-Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major theological works of Imam al-Sanusi as enumerated by his student al-Mallali, and appreciate their graded structure and significance.

Core Idea
Sanusi's theological works form a graded series, with the 'Umm al-Barahin' being the most famous.

This lesson presents the key theological writings of Imam al-Sanusi as compiled by his student al-Mallali. The list shows a systematic progression from an early commentary to the famous 'Umm al-Barahin', highlighting the depth and influence of Sanusi's contribution to Islamic theology. As you read, notice how each work builds on the previous ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic text and its English translation to get an overview of the list of works. Notice the systematic presentation by al-Mallali.
2
Identify the three main creeds
Look for the three 'aqidas: al-Kubra (كبرى), al-Wusta (وسطى), and al-Sughra (صغرى). Understand their relative lengths and that they form a graded series from longest to shortest.
3
Note the commentaries
Each major 'aqida has a commentary. Recognize that the commentaries are also significant works, with some like 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Sughra' becoming widely studied.
4
Understand the prominence of al-Sughra
The passage highlights that the Sughra, known as 'Umm al-Barahin', is the most popular and considered unparalleled. It is what is meant by 'the 'Aqida of al-Sanusi' when unqualified.

His works and his scientific legacy. The writings of Imam al-Sanusi in the Islamic library varied, and he is one of those who wrote extensively, and despite this diversity, his theological writings were a crown. And his student Sheikh al-Mallali devoted a special chapter to talking about his scientific legacy, and you will see before you all the writings he mentioned; they are: (1) First: 'al-Muqrab al-Mustawfi fi Sharh Fara'id al-Hawfi': it is his first work, and his age when he wrote it was nineteen or eighteen years, with some discrepancy in that, and his story with Sheikh al-`Arif billah al-Hasan Abran will come later, and his order to him to hide it until he reaches the age of forty. (2) 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid' or 'al-Aqida al-Kubra' (3): it is what was composed in the science of tawhid, and its expression is solid and difficult, as stated in Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta. (4) And this commentary is considered one of the most extensive theological books written by the Imam. - 'al-Aqida al-Wusta': it is more concise than 'al-Kubra' and above 'al-Sughra'. - 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta': it is among the masterpieces composed in the science of tawhid. - 'al-Aqida al-Sughra', known as 'Umm al-Barahin', 'Dhat al-Barahin', and 'al-Sanusiyya al-Sughra': it is the pearl of his 'aqa'id, and it is what is meant by their saying: (the 'Aqida of al-Sanusi) when unqualified, and it was granted a popularity that was not granted to others, and scholars approached it with commentaries, and students with memorization and study. Al-`Allama al-Mallali said: (It is among the greatest creeds, and no creed from those who came before or after equals it, and the Sheikh—may Allah be pleased with him—indicated that in the beginning of his commentary on it.) (1) - 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Sughra', also known as 'Tawhid Ahl al-`Irfan wa Ma`rifat Allah wa Rusulihi bi al-Dalil wa al-Burhan', and 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin': it also attained popularity and spread to the horizons, and how many glosses have been written upon it. - 'Sughra al-Sughra' (2): al-Mallali described it saying:
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical enumeration of the major theological works of Imam al-Sanusi, as compiled by his student al-Mallali. It begins by noting the diversity and abundance of al-Sanusi's writings, with special emphasis on his theological works. The list starts with his first work, 'al-Muqrab al-Mustawfi fi Sharh Fara'id al-Hawfi', written around age eighteen or nineteen, and includes a note that he was told to keep it hidden until forty. Next comes 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid' (or 'al-Aqida al-Kubra'), his first work in 'ilm al-tawhid, described as having a solid and difficult style. The commentary on this work, 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra' (or '`Umdat Ahl al-Tawfiq wa al-Tasdid'), is said to be one of the most extensive theological books. Then three graded 'aqidas are listed: the middle one ('al-Wusta') is more concise than the 'Kubra' but above the 'Sughra'; its commentary is a masterpiece. The most famous is 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' (known as 'Umm al-Barahin', etc.), which spread so widely that it simply referred to as 'the 'Aqida of al-Sanusi'. Al-Mallali praises it as unequalled. Its commentary, 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Sughra', also gained wide circulation. Finally, 'Sughra al-Sughra' is mentioned, described by al-Mallali. The passage thus presents a systematic overview of al-Sanusi's theological corpus, from his early work to his most famous one.

العقيدة الكبرى
العقيدة الوسطى
العقيدة الصغرى
أم البراهين
شرح العقيدة الصغرى
صغرى الصغرى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that each of Sanusi's works is an independent and unrelated text.
Correction: In reality, they form a graded series (كبرى، وسطى، صغرى) with commentaries that build on each other, showing a systematic pedagogical approach.

Checkpoint
Which of al-Sanusi's theological works is most widely studied and known simply as 'the 'Aqida of al-Sanusi'?
A) العقيدة الكبرى
B) العقيدة الوسطى
C) العقيدة الصغرى (أم البراهين)
D) صغرى الصغرى

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's theological corpus includes a graded series of creeds, with the Sughra (Umm al-Barahin) being the most widely studied and considered unparalleled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
al-Sanusi wrote his first work at 18-19 and was told to hide it until he turned forty. What hidden efforts or knowledge are you currently sitting on that you are too impatient to reveal? Are you willing to wait for the right time to share what you have learned?
?
This lesson shows a progression from a longer creed to shorter ones. Where in your own faith journey have you progressed from lengthy theological detail to a concise, firm conviction? What has your 'Umm al-Barahin' become?
?
al-Mallali claims that no creed equals al-Sanusi's Sughra. Do you approach this text with the reverence and seriousness it demands, or do you read it as just another book? What would change if you truly believed it was unparalleled?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Sanusi's Major Creedal Works and Their Commentaries
Lists Sanusi's creedal works with descriptions and significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hierarchy and purpose of Imam al-Sanusi's major creedal works, from the comprehensive to the concise, and how their commentaries support study.

Core Idea
Sanusi's creedal works form a graded curriculum for theological mastery.

Imam al-Sanusi composed several creedal texts, each tailored to a different level of study. Knowing how these works relate—from the extensive commentaries to the concise primers—helps students navigate his theological system. This passage inventories the key works and highlights their significance, especially the famous 'Umm al-Barahin'.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the works listed. Note that the passage begins by referencing a commentary (likely on al-Wusta) and then lists each work with a brief description.
This is a bibliographical list, not an argument.
2
Identify the four main works
The passage mentions four original works: al-Aqida al-Wusta (Middle Creed), al-Aqida al-Sughra (Lesser Creed), Sughra al-Sughra (Lesser of the Lesser), and al-Muqaddimat (Introductions). Find each and note their relative sizes.
Al-Sughra is the most famous, also called 'Umm al-Barahin'.
3
Notice the commentaries
Each work has a commentary written by Sanusi himself or by others. The passage praises the commentaries as extensive and valuable. See how the commentaries relate to their base texts.
Commentaries often expand on subtle points not in the original.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical purpose
Consider why Sanusi wrote multiple versions. The story behind Sughra al-Sughra shows it was for an elderly student. This illustrates that different works serve different audiences and learning needs.
The hierarchy (al-Kubra → al-Wusta → al-Sughra → Sughra al-Sughra) forms a graded sequence.

وهذا الشرح يعد من أوسع الكتب العقدية التي ألفها الإمام - العقيدة الوسطى : وهي أخصر من « الكبرى » وفوق « الصغرى » . - شرح العقيدة الوسطى : وهو من عيون ما أُلف . - « العقيدة الصغرى » المعروفة بـ « أم البراهين » و« ذات البراهين » و « السنوسية الصغرى » : وهي درّة عقائده ، والمقصودة بقولهم : « عقيدة السنوسي » عند الإطلاق ، وكُتب لها من الذيوع ما لم يكتب لغيرها ، وأقبل عليها العلماء شرحاً ، والطلاب حفظاً ودرساً ، قال العلامة الملالي : « وهي من أجل العقائد ، ولا تعادلها عقيدة من عقائد من تقدم ولا من تأخر ، وقد أشار الشيخ رضي الله عنه إلى ذلك في صدر شرحه لها » . - شرح العقيدة الصغرى ، ويعرف أيضاً بـ « توحيد أهل العرفان ومعرفة الله ورسله بالدليل والبرهان » ، وبـ « شرح أم البراهين » وهو أيضاً قد كتب له الذيوع والانتشار في الآفاق ، وكم من حاشية وضعت عليه . - « صغرى الصغرى » : وصفها الشيخ الملالي بقوله : « عقيدته المختصرة في غاية الاختصار ، وهي أصغر من الصغرى المتقدم ذكرها الآن ، ولهذا يقال لها : صغرى الصغرى ، وقد كان وضعها لوالدي حفظه الله تعالى من كل آفة وبلية ، وأناله الدرجة العلية ، وذلك أن والدي لما قرأ على الشيخ رضي الله عنه عقيدته الصغرى وختمها عليه بالتفسير غير مرة . . رأى أنه قد ثقل عليه درسها وحفظها لكبره وكثرة همومه ، فطلب من الشيخ رضي الله عنه أن يجعل له عقيدة أصغر من الصغرى ، بحيث يمكنه درسها وحفظها ، فعمل له هذه العقيدة ، وكتبها له بخطّه . وقد نبه رضي الله عنه فيها على نكت فائقة ودرر رائقة ، لم يذكرها في العقائد السابقة » . - شرح صغرى الصغرى : وهو شرح نفيس ، لا يستغني عنه طالب مستبحر ، قال الشيخ العلامة الملالي : « وفيه فوائد عجيبة ، ونكت غريبة » . - « المقدمات » ويعرف أيضاً بـ « المقدمة » : قال الشيخ الملالي : « ومنها المقدمة التي وضعها مبينة لعقيدته الصغرى ، وهي قريبة منها في الجرم ، وهي ثماني مقدمات » . - شرح المقدمات : وقراءة هذا الشرح تعد خير معين لطلاب .
And this commentary is considered one of the most extensive theological books authored by the Imam. - 'Al-Aqida al-Wusta' (The Middle Creed): it is briefer than 'al-Kubra' (The Greater) and above 'al-Sughra' (The Lesser). - Commentary on al-Aqida al-Wusta: it is one of the finest authored works. - 'Al-Aqida al-Sughra' (The Lesser Creed), known as 'Umm al-Barahin' (Mother of Proofs), 'Dhat al-Barahin' (Possessor of Proofs), and 'al-Sanusiyya al-Sughra' (The Lesser Sanusiyya): it is the pearl of his creeds, and what is meant by their saying: 'The Creed of al-Sanusi' when absolutely mentioned, and it was granted a widespread diffusion not granted to others, and scholars turned to it for commentary, and students for memorization and study. Al-Allama al-Mallali said: 'It is among the greatest creeds, and no creed before or after equals it, and the Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with him, indicated that in the beginning of his commentary on it.' - Commentary on al-Aqida al-Sughra, also known as 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan wa Ma'rifat Allah wa Rusulihi bi al-Dalil wa al-Burhan' (The Unification of the People of Gnosis and Knowledge of Allah and His Messengers by Proof and Demonstration), and 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin' (Commentary on the Mother of Proofs); it also was granted widespread diffusion across horizons, and how many glosses were written upon it. - 'Sughra al-Sughra' (The Lesser of the Lesser): Al-Mallali described it: 'His brief creed in the utmost brevity, and it is smaller than al-Sughra mentioned now, and for this reason it is called Sughra al-Sughra. It was composed for my father – may Allah preserve him from every affliction and calamity, and grant him the highest station – because when my father read al-Sughra with the Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with him, and completed it with commentary multiple times, he found teaching and memorizing it heavy due to his old age and many concerns. So he asked the Shaykh to make for him a creed smaller than al-Sughra, such that he could teach and memorize it. So he made this creed for him and wrote it in his own hand. And the Shaykh pointed out in it exquisite subtleties and brilliant pearls that he did not mention in the previous creeds.' - Commentary on Sughra al-Sughra: it is a precious commentary that a well-grounded student cannot do without. Al-Allama al-Mallali said: 'In it are wondrous benefits and strange subtleties.' - 'Al-Muqaddimat' (The Introductions), also known as 'al-Muqaddima' (The Introduction): Al-Mallali said: 'Among them is the introduction he composed explaining his al-Aqida al-Sughra; it is similar to it in size, and it is eight introductions.' - Commentary on al-Muqaddimat: Reading this commentary is the best aid for students.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical listing of Imam al-Sanusi's major creedal works and their commentaries, along with descriptions of their relative lengths and significance. The author begins by noting that the commentary under discussion (presumably Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta) is one of the most extensive theological books authored by Sanusi. He then lists 'al-Aqida al-Wusta' (the Middle Creed), which is briefer than 'al-Kubra' (the Greater) but more detailed than 'al-Sughra' (the Lesser). Next is the commentary on al-Aqida al-Wusta, described as one of the finest authored works. The most famous work is 'al-Aqida al-Sughra', known as 'Umm al-Barahin' (Mother of Proofs) and 'al-Sanusiyya al-Sughra'. The passage emphasizes its widespread acceptance and the fact that it is the default 'Creed of al-Sanusi' when mentioned absolutely. Al-Mallali is quoted praising it as unequaled by any creed before or after. The commentary on al-Sughra, also called 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin', is noted for its wide diffusion and many glosses. Then comes 'Sughra al-Sughra' (the Lesser of the Lesser), composed at the request of al-Mallali's father due to difficulty in memorizing al-Sughra. It is described as extremely brief yet containing exquisite subtleties not found in previous creeds. Its commentary is also praised. Finally, 'al-Muqaddimat' (or 'al-Muqaddima') is mentioned as an introduction to al-Sughra, consisting of eight introductions, and its commentary is recommended as an aid for students.

Key Terms

العقيدة الصغرى
أم البراهين
السنوسية الصغرى
صغرى الصغرى
المقدمات
الملالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Sughra al-Sughra is a separate or contradictory creed.
Correction: Sughra al-Sughra is a further condensation of the same creed, containing additional subtleties but no doctrinal difference.

Checkpoint
Which of Sanusi's creedal works is known as 'Umm al-Barahin' (Mother of Proofs)?
A) Al-Aqida al-Wusta
B) Al-Aqida al-Sughra
C) Sughra al-Sughra
D) Al-Muqaddimat

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's graded creedal works—from al-Wusta to Sughra al-Sughra—provide a structured path for learning Islamic theology, with al-Sughra (Umm al-Barahin) being the most widely studied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi wrote an even shorter creed specifically to help an elderly scholar. Do you adapt your learning to your current capacity, or do you push yourself with material that may be too heavy? Will you humbly adjust your studies to what you can truly absorb?
?
The commentary on Sughra al-Sughra is said to contain 'wondrous benefits' not found in larger works. Are you willing to seek out deep but accessible explanations rather than always aiming for the most comprehensive text? What keeps you from studying commentaries?
?
Sanusi's works were studied across the Muslim world. Do you have a systematic plan to learn theology step by step, or do you pick up random texts without order? Will you commit to a graded approach starting from the concise works before moving to longer ones?

Selected Works of Imam Sanusi
List of Sanusi's works with scholarly descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of Imam Sanusi's literary output, including his creedal writings, commentaries on divine names, hadith, and key terms.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's works reveal a scholar deeply engaged in creed, spirituality, and hadith.

Imam al-Sanusi was not only a theologian but a prolific author whose writings spanned creed, devotional prayers, and hadith commentary. In this lesson, we survey a list of his works as recorded by later scholars, giving us a glimpse into his scholarly legacy. The following passage presents these works with brief descriptions from al-Mallali and al-Balawi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the works
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the different titles mentioned.
This passage is a list, not an argument.
2
Understand the creed and its refutation
The first work described is a creed ('Aqida) written for some righteous people. Al-Mallali notes it contains categorical proofs against those who claim definitive effects for natural causes.
3
Discover the commentary on the Beautiful Names
Sanusi wrote a commentary on Allah's Beautiful Names. Al-Mallali mentions that after each name's explanation, Sanusi would mention the servant's share, showing influence from al-Ghazali.
4
Examine works on devotional prayers and spiritual guidance
The passage includes a commentary on the prescribed glorifications after prayer and a commentary on 'Wasitat al-Suluk', a poem by al-Hawdi.
5
Note the major hadith commentaries
Sanusi also wrote commentaries on Sahih Muslim (as a supplement) and Sahih al-Bukhari (incomplete). The passage provides details on their nature and completion status.
