عقيدة كتب بها لبعض الصالحين : قال الشيخ الملالي : ( وفي هذه العقيدة دلائل قطعية ترد على من زعم وأثبت التأثير للأسباب العادية ) . شرح أسماء الله الحسنى : قال الشيخ الملالي : ( فبعدما يذكر تفسير كل اسم من أسمائه تعالى يقول بإثره : في حظ العبد من الاسم كذا وكذا ) ، ولا يخفى تأثره بحجة الإسلام الغزالي بذلك . شرحه للتسبيح الذي حص عليه الشرع دبر كل صلاة : ذكره العلامة الملالي ، وقال : ( وهو : سبحان الله ، والحمد لله ، والله أكبر ) . شرح واسطة السلوك : و واسطة السلوك منظومة رجزية للإمام أبي عبد الله محمد بن عبد الرحمن الحوضي ، وهو مَنْ طلب من الإمام السنوسي شرحها . المنهج السديد في شرح كفاية المريد ، ويعرف أيضاً بـ شرح الجزائرية : وهو شرح لمنظومة الإمام الفقيه أبي العباس بن عبد الله الجزائري ، وقد نعت الإمام السنوسي هذا النظم في طالع كتابه بقوله : ( هو منظوم مشتمل على طريقي هداية الخواص والعوام ) ، وهي قصيدة لامية من البحر البسيط ، وعرفت أيضاً بـ الجزائرية في العقائد الإيمانية . والعلامة الناظم هو من طلب من الإمام السنوسي شرحها ، وقال العلامة البلوي : ( وهي قصيدة نفيسة بعث بها إليه من الجزائر ليشرحها ، فوضع عليها هذا الشرح الجليل وهو كبير محشو بالفوائد في علوم شتى ) . مكمّل إكمال الإكمال للإمام الأبي : وهو في شرح صحيح الإمام مسلم ، قال الشيخ الملالي : ( زاد فيه نكتاً غريبة ودرراً عجيبة ، وهو في سفرين كبيرين ) . شرح صحيح الإمام البخاري : قال الشيخ الملالي : ( ولم يكمله ) ، وذكر أنه وصل إلى ( باب من استبرأ لدينه ) . شرح مشکلات صحيح البخاري : وقعت هذه الأحاديث .
A creed written for some righteous people: Shaykh al-Mallali said: 'In this creed there are categorical proofs that refute those who claim and assert the effect of customary causes.' Commentary on the Beautiful Names of Allah: Shaykh al-Mallali said: 'After he mentions the explanation of each name of His names, he says afterwards: the servant's share of the name is such-and-such.' And his being influenced by Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali in that is not hidden. His commentary on the glorification which the Law urged after every prayer: al-Allama al-Mallali mentioned it and said: 'It is: Glory be to Allah, and praise be to Allah, and Allah is greatest.' Commentary on Wasitat al-Suluk: 'Wasitat al-Suluk' is a metrical poem (rajaz) by Imam Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Hawdi, and it is he who requested Imam al-Sanusi to comment on it. 'al-Manhaj al-Sadid fi Sharh Kifayat al-Murid,' also known as 'Sharh al-Jazairiyya': it is a commentary on a poem by the jurist Imam Abu al-Abbas ibn Abdullah al-Jazairi. Imam al-Sanusi described this poem at the beginning of his book saying: 'It is a poem including the two ways of guidance of the elite and the common people.' It is a poem in lam meter of the basit metre, and was also known as 'al-Jazairiyya in Islamic creeds.' The author of the poem is the one who requested Imam al-Sanusi to comment on it, and al-Allama al-Balawi said: 'It is a precious poem sent to him from Algeria for him to comment on, so he wrote this noble commentary on it, which is large and filled with benefits in various sciences.' 'Mukammil Ikmal al-Ikmal' by Imam al-Ubbi: it is a commentary on Sahih Imam Muslim. Shaykh al-Mallali said: 'He added rare subtleties and wonderful pearls, and it is in two large volumes.' Commentary on Sahih al-Imam al-Bukhari: Shaykh al-Mallali said: 'He did not complete it,' and mentioned that he reached 'Chapter: Whoever exercised caution for his religion.' Commentary on the Difficulties of Sahih al-Bukhari: these hadiths occurred.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical list of several works by Imam al-Sanusi, with comments from later scholars such as al-Mallali and al-Balawi. It is a record of what was written about his creedal and commentary writings. The passage opens with a creed ( عقيدة ) written for some righteous people, which al-Mallali describes as containing definitive proofs against those who claim that natural causes have an independent effect. Then it mentions a commentary on the Beautiful Names of Allah, where al-Mallali notes that after each name's explanation, al-Sanusi would mention the servant's share from that name; al-Mallali also notes al-Sanusi's influence from al-Ghazali. Next is a short commentary on the glorifications prescribed after every prayer, listing the phrases 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamdulillah, Allahu Akbar'. Then comes a commentary on 'Wasitat al-Suluk', a poem by al-Hawdi who asked al-Sanusi to write the commentary. Next is 'al-Manhaj al-Sadid', a commentary on another poem by al-Jazairi; al-Sanusi's description of the poem as covering both the elite and common ways is quoted, and al-Balawi's praise of it is given. Then 'Mukammil Ikmal al-Ikmal' by al-Ubbi is mentioned as a commentary on Sahih Muslim containing rare benefits. Finally, there are two incomplete works: a commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari that only reached a certain chapter, and a work on the difficulties of Sahih al-Bukhari that mentions these hadiths. The passage serves to document the scope and character of al-Sanusi's literary output.

‘The Straight Path in Explaining the Sufficiency of the Desirer’ – also known as ‘The Algerian Explanation’: it is an explanation of the poem of the imam jurist Abu al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abdullah al-Jaza’iri. It is a large work, extensive in knowledge.’ (4) (4) See: ‘The Holy Gifts’ (fol. 106). – ‘Explanation of the Abridgement of Imam Ibn ‘Arafah al-Warghami’ in logic: In it he solved what was difficult from the words of Imam Ibn ‘Arafah. Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of the major works written by or attributed to Imam al-Sanusi. It follows the style of a traditional scholarly biographical dictionary or catalogue of writings. The passage lists each work with a brief description, often citing the testimony of later scholars such as al-Shaykh al-Mallali or al-‘Allamah al-Balawi. The enumeration proceeds as follows:

1. The first work is ‘al-Manhaj al-Sadid fi Sharh Kifayat al-Murid,’ also known as ‘Sharh al-Jaza’iriyyah.’ It is a commentary on a poem by Abu al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abdullah al-Jaza’iri. Sanusi describes the poem as covering both the elite and common paths, and al-Balawi praises it as valuable. The footnote confirms that this commentary is large and full of benefits.
2. Next is ‘Mukammil Ikmal al-Ikmal’ by Imam al-Ubbi, a commentary on Sahih Muslim. Al-Mallali notes it contains rare subtleties and is in two large volumes. The footnote also references a modern work on Sanusi's hadith service.
3. Then ‘Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari,’ which Sanusi did not complete, reaching only the chapter on protecting one's religion.
4. ‘Sharh Mushkilat Sahih al-Bukhari’ addresses difficult hadiths at the end of Bukhari, problematic for those with weak understanding.
5. ‘Mukhtasar Sharh al-Zarkashi’ is an abridgment al-Mallali saw in Sanusi's handwriting.
6. ‘Mukhtasar Hashiyat al-Taftazani ‘ala al-Kashshaf’ is a concise abridgment since the original gloss was incomplete.
7. ‘Sharh al-Yasminiyyah’ is a commentary on a mathematical work (Introduction to Algebra) written in Sanusi's youth.
8. ‘Sharh Jumal al-Khunaji’ on logic, likely incomplete; al-Mallali saw only quires.
9. ‘Sharh Isaghuji’ on logic, attributed to al-Biqa‘i, is large and full of learning.
10. ‘Sharh Mukhtasar Ibn ‘Arafah’ on logic resolves difficult expressions of Ibn ‘Arafah.

Each work is presented with its field (hadith, logic, etc.) and often the state of completion. The frequent references to al-Mallali and al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyyah indicate that the source for this list is that work. The passage serves to document Sanusi's scholarly output, emphasizing his contributions to hadith and logic, and the fact that some works were left unfinished.

كفاية المريد
الجزائرية
مكمّل إكمال الإكمال
شرح صحيح البخاري
شرح مشکلات صحيح البخاري

مختصر حاشية التفتازاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi completed all his hadith commentaries.
Correction: The passage notes that his commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari was not completed, as al-Mallali said 'لم يكمله'.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of Sanusi's works did al-Mallali say he did not complete?

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's hadith commentaries, though some unfinished, reflect his deep engagement with prophetic traditions and the esteem of later scholars.

Sanusi's youthful work on algebra and his logic commentaries show his breadth across rational sciences.

‘The Straight Path in Explaining the Sufficiency of the Desirer’ – also known as ‘The Algerian Explanation’: it is an explanation of the poem of the imam jurist Abu al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abdullah al-Jaza’iri. Imam al-Sanusi described this poem at the beginning of his book saying: ‘It is a poem containing the two ways of guiding the elite and the commoners.’ It is a Lamiyyah poem in the al-Basit meter, and is also known as ‘The Algerian [Poem] on Doctrines of Faith.’ The author of the poem is the one who requested Imam al-Sanusi to explain it. Al-‘Allamah al-Balawi said: ‘It is a valuable poem sent to him from Algeria to explain, so he wrote this noble explanation, which is large and filled with benefits in various sciences.’ (1) See: (Register of Abu Ja‘far al-Balawi) (p. 441). ‘The Completer of the Completion of the Completion’ by Imam al-Ubbi: it is an explanation of Sahih Imam Muslim. Al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: ‘He added to it strange subtleties and wonderful gems, and it is in two large volumes.’ (2) (2) See: ‘The Holy Gifts’ (fol. 104), and ‘The Imam, the Scholar Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi and His Efforts in Serving the Noble Prophetic Hadith’ by Professor Dr. ‘Abd al-‘Aziz Dakhan. – ‘Explanation of Sahih al-Bukhari’: Al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: ‘He did not complete it,’ and mentioned that he reached ‘The chapter of whoever protects his religion.’ (3) (3) See: ‘The Holy Gifts’ (fol. 106). – ‘Explanation of the Difficult Passages of Sahih al-Bukhari’: These similar hadiths occurred at the end of it, and they are problematic for one of weak understanding and poor expression. – ‘Abridgement of al-Zarkashi’s Explanation of Sahih al-Bukhari’: Al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: ‘I saw it in his handwriting.’ (1) (1) See: ‘The Holy Gifts’ (fol. 106). – ‘Abridgement of al-Taftazani’s Gloss on al-Kashshaf’: It is likely a concise abridgment, for the ‘Gloss of Sa‘d on al-Kashshaf’ was not completed. – ‘Explanation of al-Yasminiyyah’: Al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: ‘Among them is his explanation which he wrote on the “Introduction to Algebra” by Abu Muhammad ‘Abdullah ibn Hajjaj known as Ibn al-Yasmin. It is a large work, extensive in knowledge.’ (4) (4) See: ‘The Holy Gifts’ (fol. 106). – ‘Explanation of the Abridgement of Imam Ibn ‘Arafah al-Warghami’ in logic: In it he solved what was difficult from the words of Imam Ibn ‘Arafah. Al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: ‘The Holy Gifts’ (fol. 106).
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of the major works written by or attributed to Imam al-Sanusi. It follows the style of a traditional scholarly biographical dictionary or catalogue of writings. The passage lists each work with a brief description, often citing the testimony of later scholars such as al-Shaykh al-Mallali or al-‘Allamah al-Balawi. The enumeration proceeds as follows:

1. The first work is ‘al-Manhaj al-Sadid fi Sharh Kifayat al-Murid,’ also known as ‘Sharh al-Jaza’iriyyah.’ It is a commentary on a poem by Abu al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abdullah al-Jaza’iri. Sanusi describes the poem as covering both the elite and common paths, and al-Balawi praises it as valuable. The footnote confirms that this commentary is large and full of benefits.
2. Next is ‘Mukammil Ikmal al-Ikmal’ by Imam al-Ubbi, a commentary on Sahih Muslim. Al-Mallali notes it contains rare subtleties and is in two large volumes. The footnote also references a modern work on Sanusi's hadith service.
3. Then ‘Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari,’ which Sanusi did not complete, reaching only the chapter on protecting one's religion.
4. ‘Sharh Mushkilat Sahih al-Bukhari’ addresses difficult hadiths at the end of Bukhari, problematic for those with weak understanding.
5. ‘Mukhtasar Sharh al-Zarkashi’ is an abridgment al-Mallali saw in Sanusi's handwriting.
6. ‘Mukhtasar Hashiyat al-Taftazani ‘ala al-Kashshaf’ is a concise abridgment since the original gloss was incomplete.
7. ‘Sharh al-Yasminiyyah’ is a commentary on a mathematical work (Introduction to Algebra) written in Sanusi's youth.
8. ‘Sharh Jumal al-Khunaji’ on logic, likely incomplete; al-Mallali saw only quires.
9. ‘Sharh Isaghuji’ on logic, attributed to al-Biqa‘i, is large and full of learning.
10. ‘Sharh Mukhtasar Ibn ‘Arafah’ on logic resolves difficult expressions of Ibn ‘Arafah.

Each work is presented with its field (hadith, logic, etc.) and often the state of completion. The frequent references to al-Mallali and al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyyah indicate that the source for this list is that work. The passage serves to document Sanusi's scholarly output, emphasizing his contributions to hadith and logic, and the fact that some works were left unfinished.

شرح إيساغوجي

Correction: This passage shows he also authored works on logic and mathematics, including a youthful commentary on algebra.

The Range of Sanusi's Scholarly Works
al-Mallali's enumeration of al-Sanusi's writings with notes on each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Imam al-Sanusi's scholarly output across various Islamic sciences as recorded by al-Mallali.

Core Idea
Sanusi's works spanned logic, fiqh, tafsir, and more.

After exploring Sanusi's life, we now turn to his writings—a library of works that show his mastery in multiple fields. The passage from al-Mallali's notes lists many titles, some complete, others in draft. This lesson surveys that list to appreciate his scholarly range.

Guided Path
1
Skim the list of works
Read through the Arabic passage quickly to see the sheer variety of titles mentioned. Notice the different subjects: logic, fiqh, tafsir, astronomy, and more.
This gives a sense of Sanusi's intellectual breadth.
2
Identify completion status
For each work, check whether al-Mallali mentions if it was completed, left incomplete, or only seen in draft. This tells us about Sanusi's working habits.
Some works like the commentary on Ibn 'Arafa's Mukhtasar were left unfinished due to difficulty.
3
Reflect on the purpose of the list
Ask yourself: why would a biographer include such a detailed inventory? It demonstrates Sanusi's mastery and the range of his contributions to Islamic learning.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of works attributed to or associated with Imam al-Sanusi, with annotations from Sheikh al-Mallali's work 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya'. The passage begins with a comment about something similar in its end, then lists several works: first, an abridgment of al-Zarkashi's commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari, which al-Mallali saw in the author's handwriting. Then an abridgment of al-Taftazani's gloss on al-Kashshaf, described as fine. Next, a commentary on al-Yāsamīniyya (on algebra), written in youth. Then commentaries on logical works: al-Khūnajī's Jumal (likely incomplete), Īsāghūjī (attributed to al-Biqā'ī, large and learned), and Ibn 'Arafa's Mukhtasar (difficult, sought seclusion to solve its expressions, not completed). Then al-Sanusi's own Mukhtasar in logic with additions, and his commentary on that Mukhtasar, which is sufficient for a mutakallim. Then a work on the astrolabe (with mention of his teacher al-Habbāk), an incomplete commentary on Ibn Sīnā's Arjūza, an unknown Mukhtasar on seven qirā'āt, an incomplete commentary on al-Shātibiyya al-Kubrā, and finally a commentary on al-Mudawwana in Maliki fiqh. The passage serves to catalog the scholarly output, often noting completion status and sources. The footnotes refer to al-Mallali's 'al-Mawāhib al-Qudsiyya' as the source of the quotations.

The Author's Scholarly Works: A Catalogue
Enumeration of the author's works with completion notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the breadth of the author's scholarly output and understand which works were completed or left unfinished according to his teacher al-Mallali.

Core Idea
The author's works span many fields, but many were left incomplete.

This passage is not a theological argument but a personal record from the author's teacher, listing his written works and noting whether each was completed. It reveals the author's wide-ranging interests—logic, astronomy, Qur'anic recitation, Maliki law, poetry, ethics, prophetic biography, and Sufism—and the recurring theme of incompleteness, perhaps due to death or shifting focus. Studying this list gives us insight into the scholarly priorities and challenges of a traditional North African scholar.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening remark about Ibn 'Arafa's Mukhtasar
Notice that the passage begins with a general note about the difficulty of Ibn 'Arafa's work and the author's habit of seclusion to solve its expressions, concluding that he did not complete it. This sets the theme of incompleteness.
The Mukhtasar mentioned here is not the author's own but Ibn 'Arafa's.
2
Identify each work and its completion status
Go through the list one by one. For each work, note its field (logic, astronomy, etc.) and what al-Mallali said about its completion. Some are clearly completed (e.g., al-Mukhtasar fi al-Mantiq), others incomplete, and some unknown.
There are 13 works listed. Use the translation to help.
3
Reflect on the pattern of incompleteness
Ask yourself why so many works are incomplete. Could it be that the author died young? Or that he was a perfectionist? The passage does not answer, but the pattern invites curiosity.
This connects to the learning objective.
4
Consider the range of fields covered
Notice the diversity: logic, theology (mutakallim), astronomy, qira'at, fiqh, poetry, ethics, biography, tasawwuf. This shows the author was a polymath in the Islamic sciences.
Some works are summaries or commentaries, showing the genre of scholarly writing.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخبرني الشيخ رضي الله عنه قال لي: كلام ابن عرفة صعب جداً، وخصوصاً في هذا المختصر، وكان يستعين على حل عباراته بالخلوة، ولم يكمله. المختصر في المنطق: وقد زاد فيه زيادات على جمل الخونجي. شرح المختصر في المنطق: شرح فيه كتابه السابق ذكره، وهو مما يكتفى به في هذا الفن؛ ففيه جل ما يحتاجه المتكلم. عمدة ذوي الألباب ونزهة الحساب في شرح بغية الطلاب في علم الأسطرلاب: وبغية الطلاب لشيخه الإمام أبي عبد الله الحباك. شرح أرجوزة ابن سينا: قال الشيخ الملالي: لم يكمله. مختصر في القراءات السبع: لم يعرف به الشيخ الملالي. شرح الشاطبية الكبرى: قال الشيخ الملالي: وقد رأيته بخطه غير مكمل. شرح المدونة في الفقه المالكي: قال الشيخ الملالي: شرح منها جملة كافية، وقد رأيته بخطه، ولا أدري هل كمله أم لا. شرح الوغليسية في الفقه المالكي: قال الشيخ الملالي: شرح منها شيئاً يسيراً، ولم يكمله. نظم في الفرائض: قال الشيخ الملالي: وصدره: [من الرجز] الحمد للمميت ثم الباعث الوارث الأرض وغير وارث وقد رأيته بخطه رضي الله عنه، وعمل هذا النظم في حال صغره، ولا أدري هل كمله أم لا. مختصر رعاية المحاسبي في الأخلاق والتصوف. مختصر الروض الأنف في السيرة النبوية الشريفة: وأصله للسهيلي، قال الشيخ الملالي: ولم يكمله والله أعلم. مختصر بغية السالك في أشرف المسالك في التصوف: وأصله للساحلي المعروف بالمعمم. شرح أبيات في التصوف منسوبة للإمام الإلبيري: ومطلعها: [من مخلع البسيط] رأيت ربي بقلبي فقلت لا شك أنت أنت بعين قلبي.
The shaykh (may Allah be pleased with him) informed me, saying: The speech of Ibn 'Arafa is very difficult, especially in this 'Mukhtasar', and he used to resort to seclusion to solve its expressions, and he did not complete it. 'Al-Mukhtasar fi al-Mantiq': He added additions to 'Jumal al-Khunaji'. 'Sharh al-Mukhtasar fi al-Mantiq': He explained his aforementioned book, and it is sufficient in this art; for it contains most of what the theologian (mutakallim) needs. 'Umdat dhawi al-Albab wa Nuzhat al-Hussab fi Sharh Bughyat al-Tullab fi 'Ilm al-Asturlab': and 'Bughyat al-Tullab' is by his teacher, Imam Abu 'Abd Allah al-Habbak. 'Sharh Urjuzat Ibn Sina': al-Mallali said: He did not complete it. 'Mukhtasar fi al-Qira'at al-Sab'': al-Mallali did not know it. 'Sharh al-Shatibiyya al-Kubra': al-Mallali said: I saw it in his handwriting, incomplete. 'Sharh al-Mudawwana' in Maliki fiqh: al-Mallali said: He commented on a sufficient portion of it, and I saw it in his handwriting, and I do not know whether he completed it or not. 'Sharh al-Waghlisiyya' in Maliki fiqh: al-Mallali said: He commented on a small part of it, and did not complete it. 'Nazm fi al-Fara'id': al-Mallali said: Its beginning [in rajaz]: 'Praise be to the One who causes death, then the Inheritor of the earth and not an heir'. I saw it in his handwriting, may Allah be pleased with him, and he composed this poem in his youth, and I do not know whether he completed it or not. 'Mukhtasar Ri'ayat al-Muhasibi' on ethics and Sufism. 'Mukhtasar al-Rawd al-Unuf' on the noble prophetic biography: its original is by al-Suhayli, al-Mallali said: He did not complete it, and Allah knows best. 'Mukhtasar Bughyat al-Salik fi Ashraf al-Masalik' on Sufism: its original is by al-Sahili known as al-Mu'ammam. 'Sharh Abayat fi al-Tasawwuf' attributed to Imam al-Ilbiri: its opening [in mukhalla' al-basit]: 'I saw my Lord with my heart, so I said: without doubt You are You, with my heart's eye.'
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list of the author's written works, with comments from his teacher Sheikh al-Mallali on whether each work was completed. The passage begins with a general remark about the difficulty of Ibn 'Arafa's Mukhtasar and the author's habit of retiring to seclude himself to solve its expressions, but he did not complete it. Then follows a list of works: first, a treatise on logic (Mukhtasar fi al-Mantiq) with additions to Khunaji's Jumal; second, a commentary on his own logic book (Sharh al-Mukhtasar fi al-Mantiq), praised as sufficient for theologians; third, a work on the astrolabe (Umdat dhawi al-Albab...), based on his teacher's Bughyat al-Tullab; fourth, a commentary on Ibn Sina's urjuza (unfinished); fifth, a brief work on the seven qira'at (unknown to al-Mallali); sixth, a commentary on the Shatibiyya (incomplete); seventh, a commentary on the Mudawwana in Maliki fiqh (partially completed); eighth, a commentary on the Waghlisiyya (only a small part); ninth, a poem on inheritance (composed in youth, completion unknown); tenth, a summary of al-Muhasibi's Ri'aya (no completion note); eleventh, a summary of al-Rawd al-Unuf on the Prophet's biography (unfinished); twelfth, a summary of Bughyat al-Salik on Sufism (no completion note); thirteenth, a commentary on Sufi verses attributed to al-Ilbiri (opening lines given). The list demonstrates the author's wide scholarly interests—logic, astronomy, qira'at, fiqh, poetry, ethics, biography, tasawwuf—and the recurring theme of incomplete works, suggesting either early death or shift of focus.

Al-Tha'alibi's Compilation of al-Sanusi's Commentary
Al-Sanusi's material compiled by al-Tha'alibi; mistaken attribution clarified.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a compilation of al-Sanusi's commentary on al-Aqida al-Sughra was done by his teacher al-Tha'alibi, and why it has been mistakenly attributed to al-Sanusi.

Core Idea
A teacher's compilation of a student's work is not the student's own.

This editorial note addresses a common misattribution: a compilation of al-Sanusi's explanatory material on al-Aqida al-Sughra was actually assembled by his teacher, al-Tha'alibi. The passage helps us distinguish between authorship and compilation, a key skill in studying Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the figures
Read the passage and note the two figures: al-Tha'alibi (the compiler) and al-Sanusi (the author of the source material).
2
Identify the error
The error is that some people attributed the compilation to al-Sanusi. Consider why that might happen.
3
Reflect on the editor's point
The editor concludes that despite variations in copies, the book remains beneficial and useful.

Material for his teacher, the Imam and Hafiz Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi al-Hawari, and he compiled this epistle from the commentary on al-Aqida al-Sughra (by his student Imam al-Sanusi, this commentary in which the Imam took care to explain every term current in the science of kalam). It appears that his compilation pleased his teacher Imam al-Tha'alibi, but since this material belonged to Imam al-Sanusi, some people mistakenly attributed it to him. This is what appears, and knowledge is with Allah Almighty. The observer of the widespread copies of these 'Haqa'iq' will see much variation in terms of addition and omission. Perhaps comparative attempts with the books of Imam al-Sanusi occurred, necessitating the addition of some definitions. Whatever the case, the book is beneficial and useful. - • 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan, and Knowledge of Allah and His Messengers by Proof and Demonstration': al-Baghdadi mentioned it in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin', but he noted that it is not an independent work; rather it is a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin' (1). It was previously mentioned among the works of Imam al-Sanusi, but it is mentioned here again because some people mistakenly think it is an independent work. - • (2) 'Al-Iqd al-Farid fi Hall Mushkilat al-Tawhid': al-Baghdadi said in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin': (It is a commentary on the 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri' in kalam) (3). (1) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). (2) Already mentioned (p. 23). (3) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). You already know that 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' is 'al-Minhaj al-Sadid fi Sharh Kifayat al-Murid', and it is strange that the historian al-Baghdadi mentioned it by this correct title and said it was a commentary on 'al-Jaza'iriyya'! - • 'Nusrat al-Faqir fi al-Radd 'ala Abi al-Hasan al-Saghir': al-Baghdadi also mentioned it in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (1). It appears to be one of the lengthy epistles that al-Mallali mentioned. There are separate manuscript copies of this epistle (2). It is unlikely to be an independent work by itself; rather it seems to be a fatwa that al-Sanusi was asked about regarding Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who denied allusion and symbolic expression in the way of the Sufi masters and followed the literal meaning. So al-Sanusi issued a fatwa that his books should be burned and looking into them prohibited. As for using the lack of evidence to deny attribution of this epistle or fatwa to al-Sanusi, it is a low method not relied upon by researchers. • 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa': al-Allama al-Hafnawi al-Disisi mentioned it in 'Ta'rif al-Khalaf bi Rijal al-Salaf' in the biography of (Muhammad al-Buni) where he said: (He composed the 'Aqida al-Sanusi al-Sadisa' – a creed unknown to many people – and its author, the scholar Sayyidi (1) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). It is (2) Among them is in the National Library of Algeria (146/3) and the National Library of Tunisia (1502).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note discussing the authenticity and attribution of several works associated with Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by mentioning a compilation made from al-Sanusi's commentary on 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' by his teacher al-Tha'alibi. The editor notes that although the material is al-Sanusi's, some people have mistakenly attributed the compilation to him. The editor then observes that copies of these 'Haqa'iq' vary greatly. Next, the editor lists specific works: 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is clarified as not independent but a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'. 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' is a commentary on 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri', but the editor finds it strange that al-Baghdadi correctly identifies it as a commentary yet calls it 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' which is actually a different work with the same name. 'Nusrat al-Faqir' is likely a fatwa against Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who opposed Sufi symbolism. The editor argues that denying its attribution due to lack of evidence is a weak scholarly method. Finally, 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa' is mentioned by al-Hafnawi as a little-known creed composed by al-Sanusi. The passage serves to correct misattributions and provide context for these works.

العقيدة الصغرى

Correction: It is a compilation by his teacher al-Tha'alibi from al-Sanusi's commentary.

Key Takeaway
The compilation of al-Sanusi's commentary on al-Aqida al-Sughra was made by his teacher al-Tha'alibi, not by al-Sanusi himself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
A simple mistake in attribution can cause confusion about who taught what. When you learn a new idea from a teacher or a book, do you take the time to verify its source? What habit can you develop to ensure you give credit where it is due?

Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan: Not an Independent Work
Clarification that Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan is a commentary, not an independent work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin', not an independent book.

Core Idea
Not every titled work is a separate book; some are commentaries on earlier works.

Al-Baghdadi's bibliographical dictionary 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' notes that 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is actually a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin', despite some considering it a standalone work. This lesson clarifies that confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and the claim
Find 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' in the passage and note that some people think it is independent.
2
See the correction
Al-Baghdadi clarifies it is a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'.

Source Text

مادة لشيخه الإمام الحافظ عبد الرحمن الثعالبي الهواري ، وقد جمع رسالته هذه من شرح العقيدة الصغرى ( لتلميذه الإمام السنوسي هذا الشرح الذي اعتنى فيه الإمام ببيان كل مصطلح دائر في علم الكلام ، ويظهر أنَّ جمعها قد راق لشيخه الإمام الثعالبي ، ولكن لما كانت هذه المادة للإمام السنوسي وهَم بعضهم فنسبها إليه ، هذا ما يظهر والعلم عند الله تعالى . والناظر في النسخ المنتشرة لهذه الحقائق » سيرى اختلافاً كثيراً من حيث الزيادة والنقصان ، ولعله قد وقعت محاولات مقارنة مع كتب الإمام السنوسي ألجأت إلى زيادة بعض التعريفات ، وأياً ما كان الأمر فالكتاب نافع ومفيد. - • توحيد أهل العرفان ، ومعرفة الله ورسله بالدليل والبرهان » : « ذكره البغدادي في « هدية العارفين » ، ولكن نبَّه أنه ليس تأليفاً مستقلاً ، بل هو « شرح أم البراهين شرح أم البراهين (۱) ، وقد سبق ذكره في تأليف الإمام السنوسي ، وإنما أعيد ذكره هنا لتوهم بعضهم أنه تأليف مستقل. - • (۲) العقد الفريد في حل مشكلات التوحيد » : قال البغدادي في هدية العارفين » : ( وهو شرح « لامية الجزائري ) في الكلام ) (۳) (۱) انظر » هدية العارفين » ( ٢/ ٢١٦ ) (۲) تقدم ( ص ۲۳ ) . Material for his teacher, the Imam and Hafiz Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi al-Hawari, and he compiled this epistle from the commentary on al-Aqida al-Sughra (by his student Imam al-Sanusi, this commentary in which the Imam took care to explain every term current in the science of kalam). It appears that his compilation pleased his teacher Imam al-Tha'alibi, but since this material belonged to Imam al-Sanusi, some people mistakenly attributed it to him. This is what appears, and knowledge is with Allah Almighty. The observer of the widespread copies of these 'Haqa'iq' will see much variation in terms of addition and omission. Perhaps comparative attempts with the books of Imam al-Sanusi occurred, necessitating the addition of some definitions. Whatever the case, the book is beneficial and useful. - • 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan, and Knowledge of Allah and His Messengers by Proof and Demonstration': al-Baghdadi mentioned it in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin', but he noted that it is not an independent work; rather it is a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin' (1). It was previously mentioned among the works of Imam al-Sanusi, but it is mentioned here again because some people mistakenly think it is an independent work. - • (2) 'Al-Iqd al-Farid fi Hall Mushkilat al-Tawhid': al-Baghdadi said in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin': (It is a commentary on the 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri' in kalam) (3). (1) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). (2) Already mentioned (p. 23). (3) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). You already know that 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' is 'al-Minhaj al-Sadid fi Sharh Kifayat al-Murid', and it is strange that the historian al-Baghdadi mentioned it by this correct title and said it was a commentary on 'al-Jaza'iriyya'! - • 'Nusrat al-Faqir fi al-Radd 'ala Abi al-Hasan al-Saghir': al-Baghdadi also mentioned it in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (1). It appears to be one of the lengthy epistles that al-Mallali mentioned. There are separate manuscript copies of this epistle (2). It is unlikely to be an independent work by itself; rather it seems to be a fatwa that al-Sanusi was asked about regarding Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who denied allusion and symbolic expression in the way of the Sufi masters and followed the literal meaning. So al-Sanusi issued a fatwa that his books should be burned and looking into them prohibited. As for using the lack of evidence to deny attribution of this epistle or fatwa to al-Sanusi, it is a low method not relied upon by researchers. • 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa': al-Allama al-Hafnawi al-Disisi mentioned it in 'Ta'rif al-Khalaf bi Rijal al-Salaf' in the biography of (Muhammad al-Buni) where he said: (He composed the 'Aqida al-Sanusi al-Sadisa' – a creed unknown to many people – and its author, the scholar Sayyidi (1) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). It is (2) Among them is in the National Library of Algeria (146/3) and the National Library of Tunisia (1502).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note discussing the authenticity and attribution of several works associated with Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by mentioning a compilation made from al-Sanusi's commentary on 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' by his teacher al-Tha'alibi. The editor notes that although the material is al-Sanusi's, some people have mistakenly attributed the compilation to him. The editor then observes that copies of these 'Haqa'iq' vary greatly. Next, the editor lists specific works: 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is clarified as not independent but a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'. 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' is a commentary on 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri', but the editor finds it strange that al-Baghdadi correctly identifies it as a commentary yet calls it 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' which is actually a different work with the same name. 'Nusrat al-Faqir' is likely a fatwa against Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who opposed Sufi symbolism. The editor argues that denying its attribution due to lack of evidence is a weak scholarly method. Finally, 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa' is mentioned by al-Hafnawi as a little-known creed composed by al-Sanusi. The passage serves to correct misattributions and provide context for these works.

Key Terms
توحيد أهل العرفان
شرح أم البراهين
هدية العارفين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is an independent work by al-Sanusi.
Correction: It is actually a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin', as clarified by al-Baghdadi.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baghdadi, what is 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan'?
A) An independent book on tawhid
B) A commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'
C) A fatwa against Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir
D) A poem on logic

Key Takeaway
'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is a commentary, not an independent work.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a book or lecture is completely original just because it has a unique title, without checking its relationship to earlier sources? How might this assumption distort your understanding of the Islamic tradition? Will you commit to verifying the roots of what you learn?
?
If even scholars once mistakenly thought 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' was independent, how much more careful must you be with your own knowledge? What steps will you take to ensure you do not base your beliefs on unverified assumptions?
?
The Salaf were meticulous about attribution and clarity. Are you equally careful about where you get your religious knowledge? Ask yourself: Are there any beliefs you hold that rest on a title or claim you have not investigated? Will you seek the truth even when it humbles you?

Al-Iqd al-Farid and al-Baghdadi's Error
Editor highlights an inconsistency in al-Baghdadi's description of al-Iqd al-Farid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the confusion surrounding 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' and how al-Baghdadi's attribution is problematic.

Core Idea
Bibliographical errors can propagate confusion about which work is a commentary on what.

Al-Baghdadi's entry on 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' contains an odd mistake: he says it is a commentary on 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri', yet he correctly identifies a different work as 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya'. This lesson examines that inconsistency and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the titles
Observe 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' and 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya'. See what al-Baghdadi says about each.
2
Identify the contradiction
Al-Baghdadi says 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' is a commentary on 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri', but also correctly identifies 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' as a different commentary.
3
Reflect on the editor's conclusion
The editor finds this strange and implies an error in al-Baghdadi's work.

Nusrat al-Faqir: A Fatwa on a Literalist
Explanation that Nusrat al-Faqir is a fatwa against a literalist, not a separate book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'Nusrat al-Faqir' is a fatwa by al-Sanusi against Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, and why its attribution is defended.

Core Idea
Some works are not books but fatwas; their attribution is supported by manuscript evidence.

The work 'Nusrat al-Faqir' is often misunderstood as an independent treatise. This lesson reveals it is a fatwa against a literalist opponent of Sufi symbolism, and explains why scholars accept its attribution to al-Sanusi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its subject
The work is 'Nusrat al-Faqir fi al-Radd 'ala Abi al-Hasan al-Saghir'. Note the opponent: Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir.
2
Understand the context
Abu al-Hasan rejected Sufi symbolism and followed literal interpretation. Al-Sanusi issued a fatwa ordering the burning of his books.
3
Editor's defense
The editor argues that denying attribution based on lack of evidence is a weak method, and manuscript copies exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

'Al-Iqd al-Farid' is a commentary on 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri', but the editor finds it strange that al-Baghdadi correctly identifies it as a commentary yet calls it 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' which is actually a different work with the same name. 'Nusrat al-Faqir' is likely a fatwa against Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who opposed Sufi symbolism. The editor argues that denying its attribution due to lack of evidence is a weak scholarly method. Finally, 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa' is mentioned by al-Hafnawi as a little-known creed composed by al-Sanusi. The passage serves to correct misattributions and provide context for these works.

Key Terms
نصرة الفقير
أبي الحسن الصغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nusrat al-Faqir is an independent work of theology.
Correction: It is likely a fatwa issued by al-Sanusi in response to a specific person.

Checkpoint
According to the editor, what type of work is 'Nusrat al-Faqir'?
A) An independent book on tawhid
B) A commentary on a poem
C) A fatwa against a literalist
D) A compilation of hadith

Key Takeaway
'Nusrat al-Faqir' is a fatwa by al-Sanusi against a literalist opponent of Sufi symbolism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a spiritual practice (like Sufi symbolism) as misguided without first understanding its basis? How does al-Sanusi's fatwa challenge you to be more cautious in condemning what you do not fully understand?
?
When you encounter a scholarly disagreement (e.g., between literalists and Sufis), do you tend to side with one party based on your own inclinations? What would it take for you to seek the truth with an open heart like al-Sanusi?
?
Al-Sanusi ordered the burning of books that he considered harmful. Is there any belief or habit in your life that needs to be 'burned'—decisively abandoned—because it opposes the path of Allah? What is holding you back from doing so?

Al-Aqida al-Sadisa: The Sixth Creed
Introduction of al-Aqida al-Sadisa, a little-known creed by al-Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Sanusi authored a sixth creed (al-Aqida al-Sadisa), which is less known but attested in manuscripts.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's 'Sixth Creed' exists but is not widely known.

While al-Sanusi's creeds are famous, there is a lesser-known sixth creed. This lesson examines the evidence for its existence from bibliographical sources and manuscript holdings.

Guided Path
1
Find the mention
The passage mentions al-Aqida al-Sadisa from the work of al-Hafnawi al-Disisi.
2
Note the manuscript evidence
Manuscript copies exist in the National Library of Algeria and Tunisia.

مادة لشيخه الإمام الحافظ عبد الرحمن الثعالبي الهواري ، وقد جمع رسالته هذه من شرح العقيدة الصغرى ( لتلميذه الإمام السنوسي هذا الشرح الذي اعتنى فيه الإمام ببيان كل مصطلح دائر في علم الكلام ، ويظهر أنَّ جمعها قد راق لشيخه الإمام الثعالبي ، ولكن لما كانت هذه المادة للإمام السنوسي وهَم بعضهم فنسبها إليه ، هذا ما يظهر والعلم عند الله تعالى . والناظر في النسخ المنتشرة لهذه الحقائق » سيرى اختلافاً كثيراً من حيث الزيادة والنقصان ، ولعله قد وقعت محاولات مقارنة مع كتب الإمام السنوسي ألجأت إلى زيادة بعض التعريفات ، وأياً ما كان الأمر فالكتاب نافع ومفيد. - • توحيد أهل العرفان ، ومعرفة الله ورسله بالدليل والبرهان » : « ذكره البغدادي في « هدية العارفين » ، ولكن نبَّه أنه ليس تأليفاً مستقلاً ، بل هو « شرح أم البراهين شرح أم البراهين (۱) ، وقد سبق ذكره في تأليف الإمام السنوسي ، وإنما أعيد ذكره هنا لتوهم بعضهم أنه تأليف مستقل. - • (۲) العقد الفريد في حل مشكلات التوحيد » : قال البغدادي في هدية العارفين » : ( وهو شرح « لامية الجزائري ) في الكلام ) (۳) (۱) انظر » هدية العارفين » ( ٢/ ٢١٦ ) (۲) تقدم ( ص ۲۳ ) . Material for his teacher, the Imam and Hafiz Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi al-Hawari, and he compiled this epistle from the commentary on al-Aqida al-Sughra (by his student Imam al-Sanusi, this commentary in which the Imam took care to explain every term current in the science of kalam). It appears that his compilation pleased his teacher Imam al-Tha'alibi, but since this material belonged to Imam al-Sanusi, some people mistakenly attributed it to him. This is what appears, and knowledge is with Allah Almighty. The observer of the widespread copies of these 'Haqa'iq' will see much variation in terms of addition and omission. Perhaps comparative attempts with the books of Imam al-Sanusi occurred, necessitating the addition of some definitions. Whatever the case, the book is beneficial and useful. - • 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan, and Knowledge of Allah and His Messengers by Proof and Demonstration': al-Baghdadi mentioned it in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin', but he noted that it is not an independent work; rather it is a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin' (1). It was previously mentioned among the works of Imam al-Sanusi, but it is mentioned here again because some people mistakenly think it is an independent work. - • (2) 'Al-Iqd al-Farid fi Hall Mushkilat al-Tawhid': al-Baghdadi said in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin': (It is a commentary on the 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri' in kalam) (3). (1) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). (2) Already mentioned (p. 23). (3) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). You already know that 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' is 'al-Minhaj al-Sadid fi Sharh Kifayat al-Murid', and it is strange that the historian al-Baghdadi mentioned it by this correct title and said it was a commentary on 'al-Jaza'iriyya'! - • 'Nusrat al-Faqir fi al-Radd 'ala Abi al-Hasan al-Saghir': al-Baghdadi also mentioned it in 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (1). It appears to be one of the lengthy epistles that al-Mallali mentioned. There are separate manuscript copies of this epistle (2). It is unlikely to be an independent work by itself; rather it seems to be a fatwa that al-Sanusi was asked about regarding Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who denied allusion and symbolic expression in the way of the Sufi masters and followed the literal meaning. So al-Sanusi issued a fatwa that his books should be burned and looking into them prohibited. As for using the lack of evidence to deny attribution of this epistle or fatwa to al-Sanusi, it is a low method not relied upon by researchers. • 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa': al-Allama al-Hafnawi al-Disisi mentioned it in 'Ta'rif al-Khalaf bi Rijal al-Salaf' in the biography of (Muhammad al-Buni) where he said: (He composed the 'Aqida al-Sanusi al-Sadisa' – a creed unknown to many people – and its author, the scholar Sayyidi (1) See 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' (2/216). It is (2) Among them is in the National Library of Algeria (146/3) and the National Library of Tunisia (1502).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note discussing the authenticity and attribution of several works associated with Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by mentioning a compilation made from al-Sanusi's commentary on 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' by his teacher al-Tha'alibi. The editor notes that although the material is al-Sanusi's, some people have mistakenly attributed the compilation to him. The editor then observes that copies of these 'Haqa'iq' vary greatly. Next, the editor lists specific works: 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan' is clarified as not independent but a commentary on 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'. 'Al-Iqd al-Farid' is a commentary on 'Lamyyat al-Jaza'iri', but the editor finds it strange that al-Baghdadi correctly identifies it as a commentary yet calls it 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' which is actually a different work with the same name. 'Nusrat al-Faqir' is likely a fatwa against Abu al-Hasan al-Saghir, who opposed Sufi symbolism. The editor argues that denying its attribution due to lack of evidence is a weak scholarly method. Finally, 'al-Aqida al-Sadisa' is mentioned by al-Hafnawi as a little-known creed composed by al-Sanusi. The passage serves to correct misattributions and provide context for these works.

Titles and Description of the Concise Creed
Lists the titles and describes the creed's conciseness and clarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various titles of al-Sanusi's concise creed and the characteristics that make it accessible to all audiences.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's creed is known by many names, all pointing to its brevity and clarity.

Before delving into the content of al-Sanusi's concise creed, it is helpful to know its various names and why it was composed. This passage lists the titles and describes the creed's remarkable conciseness and clarity, setting the stage for understanding its purpose.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overall sense of the content.
Pay attention to the list of titles and the description that follows.
2
Identify the different titles
Note each title mentioned in the passage: al-Sughra, Sughra al-Sughra, al-Hafida, 'Aqidat al-Nisa', 'Aqidat al-Niswan wa al-Sibyan, and al-Wajiza. Understand that these all refer to the same work.
Some titles highlight the creed's size, others its intended audience.
3
Understand the description of the creed
Examine how the creed is described: elegant, no more than two pages, easy in expression, clear in proofs, and accessible to all minds.
This description reinforces why it was composed for women and children.
4
Reflect on the intended audience
Consider the statement from Abd al-Rahman al-Jami'i that it was written for women and children. How does this relate to the creed's simplicity?
Think about the pedagogical purpose of such a concise work.

عبد الرحمن الجامعي ، قيل : إنَّ الشيخ وضعها للنسوان والصبيان )(١) وترتبط بهذه « العقيدة » أعلام أخرى أطلقت عليها ، يجدر إيرادها قبل الحديث عنها ؛ وهي : صغریٰ صغرى الصغرى » العقيدة الحفيدة » عقيدة النساء » عقيدة النسوان والصبيان » العقيدة الوجيزة » وهذه العناوين كلُّها لعقيدة لطيفة جدّاً ، لا تتجاوز الصفحتين ، سهلة العبارة ، واضحة الدلائل ، قريبة ـ كما وصفت ـ من جميع الأذهان على تفاوت فهومها
Abd al-Rahman al-Jami'i said: It is said that the Shaykh (al-Sanusi) composed it for women and children. And associated with this 'creed' are other appellations given to it, which it is proper to mention before discussing it: they are: al-Sughra, Sughra al-Sughra, al-'Aqida al-Hafida, 'Aqidat al-Nisa', 'Aqidat al-Niswan wa al-Sibyan, al-'Aqida al-Wajiza. And all of these titles refer to a very elegant creed, not exceeding two pages, easy in expression, clear in evidence, close (as described) to all minds despite the differences in their understandings.

Commentary
This passage provides an introduction to a concise creed attributed to Imam al-Sanusi. It begins with a statement from Abd al-Rahman al-Jami'i that the creed was composed for women and children, indicating its intended audience and simplicity. Then it lists the various names by which this creed is known: 'al-Sughra' (the Smaller), 'Sughra al-Sughra' (the Smaller of the Smaller), 'al-Hafida' (the Granddaughter), 'Creed of Women', 'Creed of Women and Children', and 'the Concise Creed'. After listing the titles, the passage describes the creed's characteristics: it is very elegant, no longer than two pages, easy in wording, clear in proofs, and accessible to all minds regardless of their varying levels of comprehension.

Attribution of the Creed to al-Sanusi: Evidence and Praise
Discusses evidence for the creed's attribution and quotes scholars' praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars established the attribution of the 'Hafida' creed to Imam al-Sanusi through historical evidence and scholarly praise.

Core Idea
Scholarly confidence in attribution comes from early commentaries and unanimous praise.

This lesson examines the historical evidence for the attribution of the concise creed known as 'al-Hafida' to Imam al-Sanusi. While no single definitive proof exists, the multiplicity of early commentaries and the consistent wording across them provide strong circumstantial evidence. Additionally, we will explore the glowing endorsements of al-Sanusi's works by later scholars, which further solidify his authorship.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of attribution
Read the opening lines where the author admits there is no definitive proof for the creed's attribution, but a text from al-Hafnawi is the basis. Notice the cautious tone.
This sets up the evidential challenge.
2
Examine the positive evidence
Focus on the three factors: multiplicity of commentaries, agreement of expressions, and early dates (11th century AH). The author says these may make us trust the attribution.
These are circumstantial but cumulative.
3
Consider al-Saketani's caution
Read al-Saketani's statement that the creed was 'among what was attributed' to al-Sanusi. The author says this is fair and investigative, showing caution but not denying attribution.
This shows scholarly integrity.
4
Learn the scholarly praises
Read the quotes from al-Shafshawni and al-Hubti praising al-Sanusi's works as flawless and accepted by all. These endorsements support the reliability of his writings.
These quotes reinforce the positive assessment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن لا مستند يقطع بنسبة هذه العقيدة المباركة المتفق على ما فيها إلى الإمام السنوسي ، بل النص المنقول إليك عن العلامة الحفناوي هو الذي دار عليه المتأخّرون في إثباتها نعم ؛ تعدد شروحها ، واتفاق عباراتها ، وتقدم هذه الشروح تاريخياً ؛ إذ يعودُ كثير منها إلى مطلع القرن الحادي عشر الهجري إلى منتصفه . . قد يجعلنا نثق بنسبتها إلى الإمام السنوسي ، على أن الإمام السكتاني - وهو واحد من شرّاحها - اكتفى بقوله : ( وكان من جملة ما نُسب إليه ـ يعني : الإمام السنوسي العقيدة المسماة بـ « الحفيدة » ( ۱ ) . وهذه من الإمام الشكتاني كلمة إنصاف وتحقيق ، ولو كان بين يديه حينها ما يؤكِّد نسبتها إلى الإمام السنوسي . . لجزم وقطع بذلك لكنه اكتفى بهذه العبارة المشككة ، ولم يعبأ بهذا التشكيك مع حسن عبارة هذه العقيدة ووجازتها وقرب مأخذها ( شرح الموجهات » في المنطق : ولعله جزء من أحد كتبه المنطقية ؛ إذ الموجهات من أبحاثه رسالة في الطب » أو « شرح حديث : المعدة بيت الداء » : وهو كتابه في شرح أرجوزة ابن سينا » في الطب وقد تقف على بعض العناوين الأخرى منسوبة إلى الإمام السنوسي وهي مما يُقطع بعدم نسبتها إليه ، فلا داعي للتعرض لها وقد وصف الشفشاوني تأليف الإمام السنوسي بكلمة جامعة فقال : ( ناهيك بتنوير كلامه ، وإتقان عبارته ، حتى لا يجد المتعسف مدخلاً للتعقب بوجه ولا بحال ، واتفاقِ فحول الأولياء وأكابر العلماء على فضله وتلقي تآليفه بالقبول )(۲) ونقل عن الإمام أبي عبد الله الهبطي قوله : ( كلام السنوسي محفوظ من السقطات )(۳)
But there is no definitive proof for the attribution of this blessed creed (whose contents are agreed upon) to Imam al-Sanusi. Rather, the text transmitted to you from the scholar al-Hafnawi is what the later scholars relied upon for establishing it. Yes, the multiplicity of its commentaries, the agreement of their expressions, and the historical precedence of these commentaries – for many of them date from the beginning of the eleventh century AH to its middle – may make us trust its attribution to Imam al-Sanusi. However, Imam al-Saketani – and he is one of its commentators – contented himself with saying: 'Among what was attributed to him – meaning Imam al-Sanusi – is the creed called al-Hafida.' This statement from al-Saketani is a word of fairness and verification; if he had had in his hands something that confirmed its attribution to Imam al-Sanusi, he would have asserted and affirmed it, but he contented himself with this equivocal expression. And he did not care about this uncertainty given the goodness of this creed's wording, its conciseness, and the accessibility of its derivation. (Sharh al-Muwajjahat in logic: perhaps it is part of one of his logical works, for al-Muwajjahat are among his researches. A treatise on medicine, or Sharh Hadith 'al-Mi'da Bayt al-Da'', which is his book commenting on Ibn Sina's Urjuza on medicine. And you may come across other titles attributed to Imam al-Sanusi which are definitively not attributable to him, so there is no need to address them.) And al-Shafshawni described the works of Imam al-Sanusi with a comprehensive statement, saying: 'Sufficient for you is the illumination of his speech, the perfection of his expression, so that the obtuse person finds no avenue for objection in any way or manner, and the agreement of the eminent saints and great scholars on his virtue and the acceptance of his works.' And it is narrated from Imam Abu Abd Allah al-Hubti that he said: 'The speech of al-Sanusi is preserved from slips.'
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of attribution of the concise creed to Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by acknowledging that there is no definitive evidence proving that the creed is from al-Sanusi. However, the text that was cited from al-Hafnawi is the basis upon which later scholars relied. The author then presents supporting arguments: the existence of many commentaries, the consistency of their wording, and the early dates of these commentaries (many from the early to mid-11th century AH) collectively encourage confidence in the attribution. The passage then mentions Imam al-Saketani, one of the commentators, who only said it was 'among what was attributed' to al-Sanusi, indicating caution. The author comments that al-Saketani's statement is fair and investigative; if he had had proof, he would have stated it definitively, but he did not. The author dismisses any doubt because of the creed's excellent wording and accessibility. Then the passage briefly lists other works attributed to al-Sanusi (in logic and medicine) but notes that some are definitively not his and need not be discussed. Finally, the passage quotes two scholars praising al-Sanusi's works: al-Shafshawni says his speech is luminous and flawless, so no one can object, and al-Hubti says his speech is preserved from mistakes. This overall passage establishes the reliability of al-Sanusi's writings despite some uncertainties.

شراح
الحفيدة
الشكتاني
الشفشاوني
الهبطي

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author trusts the creed partly because of its beauty and conciseness. Have you ever dismissed a teaching because it was difficult or uncomfortable? Could its beauty and depth be a sign of its truth, as here, and your resistance be a sign of your own need to grow?
?
Al-Saketani's cautious 'attributed' challenges the reader to consider intellectual honesty. Where in your own life do you hold back from asserting something without full certainty, and where do you lack the courage to admit uncertainty? What would it mean to be as fair and investigative as al-Saketani?

Sanusi's Key Works and Authentic Attribution
Lists al-Sanusi's works and warns against false attributions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two authentic works of Imam al-Sanusi and why scholars caution against false attributions.

Core Idea
Authentic attribution is the bedrock of reliable scholarship.

This passage introduces us to two of Imam al-Sanusi's authentic works: one in logic (Sharh al-Muwajjahat) and one in medicine (a commentary on Ibn Sina's arjuzah). It also issues a stern warning about other titles falsely attributed to him, teaching us that not every book bearing a scholar's name is genuinely his. Verifying authorship is an essential part of Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original text and its English translation carefully. Note the two works mentioned and the warning that follows.
Pay attention to the phrase 'يُقطع بعدم نسبتها إليه' — it expresses certainty about false attribution.
2
Identify the two works
The passage names a logical work (Sharh al-Muwajjahat) and a medical work (a treatise or commentary on the hadith about the stomach). Understand what each work is about from the commentary.
3
Understand the warning
The author states that other titles attributed to al-Sanusi are certainly not his and need not be mentioned. This highlights the importance of textual criticism in Islamic scholarship.
4
Reflect on scholarly diligence
Consider why scholars take such care to distinguish authentic works from forgeries. How does this protect the tradition?
False attributions can lead to incorrect knowledge about a scholar's positions.

Commentary
This passage lists two of Imam al-Sanusi's works: 'Sharh al-Muwajjahat' (Explanation of Modal Propositions) in logic, and a medical work which is either a treatise on medicine or a commentary on the hadith about the stomach. The author also warns that other works are falsely attributed to al-Sanusi and should be disregarded. This shows scholarly concern for authentic attribution.

Praise of Sanusi's Writings by Two Scholars
Praise of Sanusi's writings by al-Shifshawni and al-Habti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two notable scholars—al-Shifshawni and al-Habti—affirmed the excellence and error-free nature of Imam al-Sanusi's writings, establishing the authority of his works in the tradition.

Core Idea
Scholarly praise confirms that Sanusi's writings are both perfect in expression and free from errors.

Imam al-Sanusi's theological works are foundational in the Ash'ari tradition. To underscore their authority, later scholars often quote the endorsements of earlier masters. This lesson presents two such endorsements: one from al-Shifshawni and one from al-Habti, each highlighting a different dimension of Sanusi's scholarly excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two separate quotes and how they are introduced.
2
Identify the two testimonials
The passage contains two distinct praises: one from al-Shifshawni and one from al-Habti. Note what each scholar emphasizes about Sanusi's writings.
Al-Shifshawni focuses on completeness and acceptance; al-Habti focuses on errorlessness.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why these testimonies are included in a theological text. What function does such praise serve in establishing the authority of the work?
This connects to the overall aim of the course: learning from authoritative sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد وصف الشفشاوني تأليف الإمام السنوسي بكلمة جامعة فقال : ( ناهيك بتنوير كلامه ، وإتقان عبارته ، حتى لا يجد المتعسف مدخلاً للتعقب بوجه ولا بحال ، واتفاقِ فحول الأولياء وأكابر العلماء على فضله وتلقي تآليفه بالقبول )(۲) ونقل عن الإمام أبي عبد الله الهبطي قوله : ( كلام السنوسي محفوظ من السقطات )(۳)
And al-Shifshawni described the authorship of Imam al-Sanusi with a comprehensive statement, saying: 'It is sufficient that his speech is illuminating, his expression is perfect, so that the oppressor finds no way to criticize in any manner or state, and the agreement of the great saints and senior scholars on his virtue and acceptance of his works.' And he narrated from Imam Abu 'Abdullah al-Habti his saying: 'The speech of al-Sanusi is preserved from slips.'
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents two testimonials praising Imam al-Sanusi's writings. Al-Shifshawni emphasizes the clarity and precision of Sanusi's language, such that even those seeking to find fault cannot. Al-Habti adds that Sanusi's speech is free from errors (saqatat). These quotes serve to establish the scholarly authority of Sanusi's works.

Key Terms
الشفشاوني
الهبطي
قبول
السقطات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The praise refers to al-Sanusi's personal spoken speech rather than his written works.
Correction: Both scholars are specifically praising his writings (tā'līf, tā'līfihī), not his extemporaneous speech.

Checkpoint

A) They are difficult to understand.
B) They are perfect and immune to criticism.
C) They are only for specialists.
D) They contain some errors.

Key Takeaway
Two renowned scholars, al-Shifshawni and al-Habti, testified that Imam al-Sanusi's writings are flawlessly expressed and free from error, securing their acceptance among scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own words about the deen were examined by the 'great saints and senior scholars', would they be 'preserved from slips'? What 'saqatat' might they find, and what are you willing to correct today?
?
Al-Shifshawni says Sanusi's expression is so perfect that even the oppressor finds no way to criticize. Is your own speech in matters of faith equally careful, or do you leave room for ambiguity? What one change in how you speak about Allah can you commit to this week?
?
The scholars accepted Sanusi's works unanimously. Do you seek the approval of such righteous authorities, or do you more often crave the praise of those who flatter you? How can you shift your pursuit from popular acclaim to the approval of the 'فحول الأولياء وأكابر العلماء'?

Sanusi's Noble Character
Describes Sanusi's character with a list of virtues and a luminous summary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the noble character traits of Imam al-Sanusi as described by his biographers.

Core Idea
Sanusi's character was a luminous mold of mercy, humility, and devotion.

This passage offers a glimpse into the personal qualities of Imam al-Sanusi, highlighting his piety, compassion, and humility. Before reading his scholarly works, it is valuable to appreciate the moral character that underlies his intellectual contributions.

Guided Path
1
Read the character description
Read the Arabic text describing Sanusi's character. Notice the list of virtues and the summary statement about his luminous mold.
The passage uses vivid imagery like 'pitched his tents'.
2
Reflect on each virtue
Consider what each trait means: good, pious, ascetic, patient, etc. How do these qualities relate to his role as a scholar?
These traits are interconnected—humility supports mercy, etc.
3
Connect to the summary
The passage ends with 'his mold was luminous' — what does that imply about his nature? Relate it to the earlier description.
This summary elevates the description from mere actions to intrinsic nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبس من عظیم اخلاقه جمع الله تعالى للإمام السنوسي إلى عظيم علمه وبحبوحة معرفتِهِ . . سعة الأخلاق الحميدة ، فجابَ شُعب الإيمان وطنَّبَ فيها خيامه ، فعُهِدَ عنه أنه خيرٌ بر ، تقي ورع زاهد ، حلیم صبور ، سكنتِ الرحمة فؤاده ، وغلبت عليه الشفقة على جميع خلق الله تعالى ، هين لين القياد ، شديد الحياء ، كثير التواضع ، قليل الكلام والضحك تجلّى عليه الخوف من الله تعالى ؛ فأكثر من إحياء الليل مناجياً ، وأكثر من الصدقة والدعاء راجياً . وبالجملة : كانت طينته نورانية ، وسيرته محفوفة بعناية ربانية أمَّا سعة علمه : فآثاره العلمية الواسعة تشهد له بذلك ، ولا سيما علم التوحيد والتصوف قال فيه العلامة الشفشاوني : ( كان من مشايخ المئة التاسعة ، وتوفي على رأسها ، فكان من جدَّد لهذه الأمة أمر دينها على رأس تلك المئة كما أخبر الصادق المصدوق صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وكان من أكابر الأولياء ، وأعلام العلماء ، وتآليفه تدلُّ على تحقيقه وغزارة علمه )(۱)
A gleam from his great character: Allah Almighty gathered for Imam al-Sanusi, along with his immense knowledge and expanse of his gnosis, broad noble character. So he traversed the branches of faith and pitched his tents therein. It was known about him that he was good, pious, God-fearing, ascetic, forbearing, patient. Mercy settled in his heart, and compassion for all of Allah's creation dominated him. Gentle, easy to lead, extremely shy, very humble, little in speech and laughter. The fear of Allah was manifest upon him, so he would frequently revive the night in intimate conversation (munajat), and would frequently give charity and supplicate, hoping. In summary: his mold (tinah) was luminous, and his conduct was encompassed by divine care. As for his vast knowledge: his extensive scholarly works testify to that, especially the sciences of tawhid (monotheism) and tasawwuf (Sufism). Al-'Allama al-Shifshawni said about him: 'He was one of the shaykhs of the ninth century (hijri), and he died at its beginning. He was one of those who renewed for this nation the affairs of its religion at the head of that century, as the truthful and believed (Prophet) peace be upon him informed. And he was among the greatest saints and foremost scholars, and his writings indicate his verification (tahqiq) and abundance of knowledge.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage first describes Imam al-Sanusi's character in detail, listing many virtues: piety, asceticism, humility, mercy, and fear of Allah. It then discusses his knowledge, emphasizing his works in tawhid and tasawwuf. The passage concludes with a quote from al-Shifshawni, who places Sanusi among the renewers (mujaddids) of the ninth century, citing his scholarly achievements and saintly status. The passage functions as a comprehensive biographical sketch, combining moral and intellectual qualities.

الشفقة
الورع

A) Fear
B) Mercy

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's character was marked by mercy, piety, and humility, forming a luminous foundation for his scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Sanusi frequently revived the night in intimate conversation with Allah. When was the last time your prayer felt like a real conversation, not just routine? Will you set aside 10 minutes tonight to speak to Him with your heart?
?

Sanusi's Exemplary Character and Piety
Describes Sanusi's excellent moral character and devotion

Learning Objective

Core Idea
A scholar's true worth is shown in his character, not just his knowledge.

This lesson presents a biographical sketch of Imam al-Sanusi that goes beyond his scholarly achievements. It paints a picture of his moral and spiritual character, emphasizing that his knowledge was matched by his piety, mercy, humility, and devotion. The passage serves as a model of the integrated Islamic personality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow: an opening statement, a list of virtues, and a concluding summary.
The passage uses a series of adjectives and phrases to describe Sanusi's character.
2
Identify the key virtues

The virtues are not ranked; they form a holistic picture.
3

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبس من عظیم اخلاقه جمع الله تعالى للإمام السنوسي إلى عظيم علمه وبحبوحة معرفتِهِ . . سعة الأخلاق الحميدة ، فجابَ شُعب الإيمان وطنَّبَ فيها خيامه ، فعُهِدَ عنه أنه خيرٌ بر، تقي ورع زاهد، حلیم صبور، سكنتِ الرحمة فؤاده، وغلبت عليه الشفقة على جميع خلق الله تعالى، هين لين القياد، شديد الحياء، كثير التواضع، قليل الكلام والضحك تجلّى عليه الخوف من الله تعالى؛ فأكثر من إحياء الليل مناجياً، وأكثر من الصدقة والدعاء راجياً. وبالجملة: كانت طينته نورانية، وسيرته محفوفة بعناية ربانية

?

?

?

Sanusi's Vast Knowledge and the Testimony of al-Shafshawani
States Sanusi's vast knowledge and quotes al-Shafshawani's praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi's scholarly works and the testimony of al-Shafshawani establish his vast knowledge and role as a mujaddid.

Core Idea
Sanusi's works and a scholar's praise confirm his role as a renewer of religion.

This passage highlights the evidence for Sanusi's vast knowledge, especially in tawheed and tasawwuf, and presents a powerful testimony from al-Shafshawani, who declares Sanusi a mujaddid (renewer) of the ninth century. This lesson unpacks that testimony and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice how the biographer first states a claim, then supports it with a quote.
The quote from al-Shafshawani is the core of this passage.
2
Identify the two pieces of evidence
The biographer presents two evidences: (1) Sanusi's extensive scholarly works, especially in tawheed and tasawwuf, and (2) the testimony of al-Shafshawani. Find each in the text.
Al-Shafshawani's testimony includes multiple points: Sanusi was a shaykh of the ninth century, a mujaddid, a great saint, and a leading scholar.
3
Understand the concept of tajdid (renewal)
Al-Shafshawani says Sanusi was 'among those who renewed for this nation the matter of its religion'. Reflect on the hadith about a renewer at the turn of every century, and why being a mujaddid is a high honor.
The 'truthful and believed' refers to the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) and his hadith on tajdid.
4
Connect scholarship and sainthood
Al-Shafshawani calls Sanusi both a great saint (akābir al-awliyā') and a leading scholar (a‘lām al-‘ulamā'). Notice that sainthood and scholarship are not separate; his works indicate both his verification and abundance of knowledge.
This shows that deep knowledge leads to spiritual rank in the Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا سعة علمه: فآثاره العلمية الواسعة تشهد له بذلك، ولا سيما علم التوحيد والتصوف. قال فيه العلامة الشفشاوني: ( كان من مشايخ المئة التاسعة، وتوفي على رأسها، فكان من جدَّد لهذه الأمة أمر دينها على رأس تلك المئة كما أخبر الصادق المصدوق صلى الله عليه وسلم، وكان من أكابر الأولياء، وأعلام العلماء، وتآليفه تدلُّ على تحقيقه وغزارة علمه )
As for the vastness of his knowledge: his extensive scholarly works testify to that, especially the science of tawheed (theology) and tasawwuf (spirituality). The scholar al-Shafshawani said about him: 'He was among the shaykhs of the ninth century (AH), and he died at its beginning, so he was among those who renewed for this nation the matter of its religion at the beginning of that century, as the truthful and believed (Prophet) صلى الله عليه وسلم informed, and he was among the greatest saints and leading scholars, and his works indicate his verification and abundance of knowledge.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage opens the section on Sanusi's knowledge. The biographer first asserts that his many scholarly works are evidence, especially in tawheed and tasawwuf. Then he quotes al-Shafshawani, who places Sanusi among the mujaddids (renewers) of the ninth century, affirms his sainthood and scholarship, and notes that his writings prove his depth and breadth.

Checkpoint
According to al-Shafshawani, what role did Sanusi fulfil at the beginning of the ninth century?
A) He was a judge
B) He was a renewer (mujaddid) of the religion
C) He was a governor
D) He was a trader

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's vast knowledge is evidenced by his scholarly works and the testimony of al-Shafshawani, who affirms him as a mujaddid and a great saint.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Sanusi's works testify to his vast knowledge, what do your own works — your studies, your time, your conversations — testify to? Is your life producing evidence of a heart devoted to tawheed and tasawwuf?
?
Al-Shafshawani called Sanusi a mujaddid because he renewed the matter of religion. What part of your faith feels stagnant or in need of renewal? Will you take one step today to revive that area, even if it's small?
?
Sanusi was both a scholar and a saint. Are you pursuing knowledge that transforms your soul, or just fills your mind? Which one are you neglecting, and what will you do to restore the balance?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
The True Scholar: Al-Hadiki's Praise of Sanusi and Sanusi's Own Definition
Al-Hadiki's praise of Sanusi and Sanusi's definition of a true scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the qualities of a true scholar as exemplified by Imam Sanusi, including both external testimony and his own criterion.

Core Idea
A true scholar finds complexity in the obvious and clarifies the obscure.

This passage presents a vivid portrait of what a scholar should be: first, through the eyes of a contemporary, al-Hadiki, who describes Sanusi's unparalleled mastery; then, through Sanusi's own succinct definition. Together, they provide a model of scholarly excellence that combines depth of knowledge, mindfulness of Allah, and the ability to illuminate difficult subjects.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Hadiki's testimony
Read the first part where al-Hadiki describes Sanusi's extraordinary knowledge and piety. Notice the specific sciences mentioned and the effect on listeners.
Al-Hadiki emphasizes Sanusi's mastery in tawheed and his unique insight into the esoteric sciences.
2
Identify key attributes
List the attributes al-Hadiki ascribes to Sanusi: a sign in knowledge, righteousness, guidance, asceticism, piety, and ability to focus on the afterlife.
These attributes together paint a picture of a complete scholar.
3
Examine Sanusi's definition
Read Sanusi's definition of a true scholar: one who finds the clear to be problematic and clarifies the problematic due to breadth of understanding.
This definition emphasizes deep critical thinking, not superficial acceptance.
4
Reflect on the connection
Consider how al-Hadiki's description exemplifies Sanusi's own definition. How does Sanusi's life match his criteria?
Sanusi himself embodied the definition he gives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال العلامة الحضيكي: ( كان آية في العلم والصلاح والهدى والزهد والورع، له أوفر حظ في العلوم فروعها وأصولها، إذا تحدث في علم ظنَّ السامع أنه لا يحسن غيره، لا سيما في التوحيد، وانفرد بعلم الباطن، لا يقرأ شيئاً من علم الظاهر إلا خرج لعلوم الآخرة لا سيما في التفسير والحديث، كأنه يشاهد الآخرة؛ لكثرة مراقبته الله تعالى ). وقد جعل رحمه الله تعالى للعالم علامات يعرف بها؛ حيث قال: ( العالم حقاً: من يستشكل الواضح، ويوضح المشكل؛ لسعة فهمه وعلمه وتحقيقه، فهو الذي يُحضر مجلسه، ويُستمع فوائده )
And the scholar al-Hadiki said: 'He was a sign in knowledge, righteousness, guidance, asceticism, and piety. He had the most abundant share in the sciences, both branches and roots. When he spoke about a science, the listener would think he excelled in no other, especially in tawheed. He was unique in the esoteric science (ilm al-batin). He would not read anything of the exoteric science (ilm al-zahir) without drawing out lessons for the afterlife, especially in tafsir (Quranic exegesis) and hadith, as if he witnessed the afterlife due to his abundant mindfulness of Allah the Exalted.' And he (Sanusi) may Allah have mercy on him set signs by which the scholar is known, saying: 'The true scholar is the one who finds the clear to be problematic and clarifies the problematic, due to the breadth of his understanding, knowledge, and verification. So he is the one whose gathering is attended and whose benefits are listened to.'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts. First, al-Hadiki's testimony elaborates on Sanusi's unparalleled mastery in both exoteric and esoteric sciences, especially tawheed, and his ability to derive afterlife lessons from all exoteric knowledge. Second, Sanusi's own definition of a true scholar: one who perceives difficulty in what seems obvious (because he sees deeper issues) and solves difficult problems, thereby attracting students to his gatherings for their benefit.

Key Terms
آية
الصلاح
الهدى
علم الباطن
علم الظاهر
المراقبة
علامات العالم
يستشكل الواضح
يوضح المشكل
سعة الفهم
التحقيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'yastashkilu al-wadih' (finds the clear problematic) is sometimes misinterpreted as doubting clear truths or rejecting obvious facts.
Correction: Actually, it means recognizing subtle complexities and deeper dimensions in matters that appear simple, which requires deep insight and knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what kind of person deserves to have his gathering attended and benefits listened to?
A) He who has many books
B) He who is a true scholar
C) He who is rich
D) He who is old

Key Takeaway
A true scholar is one who sees depth in apparent clarity and clarifies challenges, attracting seekers of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read something in the Quran or a book that seems clear, do you ever pause and ask, 'What might I be missing?' Or do you move on satisfied? Which habit brings you closer to being the scholar Sanusi described?
?
Sanusi was known for extracting lessons for the afterlife from every exoteric text. If you examine your own study of tafsir and hadith, are you truly seeking akhirah, or are you accumulating information for this world? What would change if you started reading each verse as if it were a direct message to your soul?
?
The true scholar 'is the one whose gathering is attended and whose benefits are listened to.' Do you have a circle of seekers around you because of your knowledge? If not, why? Is it because your knowledge lacks depth or because you have not yet become the kind of scholar who sees problems and clarifies them? What step can you take today to change that?
